Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the moon as we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not help at all, then there are three ways of cauterization that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of these there is one method in which you make three cauteries, or four, by tracing according to the length of the mole, according to the shape of the cautery which we mentioned before; and do not press your hand on the cautery throughout, and let the patient be careful on his back; and another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two points, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the curve where the mole is, or where the pain comes from towards the left, and let the elevation by which you lift the curve be according to the curve, according to the length of the body, and let the cautery be according to the breadth of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Afterwards, insert the two flaming points until the curve is pierced from the other side; and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four of them. And if you wish, you can cauterize throughout with three points.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has healed scabs for a long time, and this happens more than any of the other cures mentioned earlier.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not effective for hydrophobia, except in the manner which is called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure it according to the methods we have discussed in sections, and your cure is not effective, then you should do three cauterizations around the armpit, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the breast, two behind the back on the spine, and one in the groin; the cautery should be close to the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery open to drain pus for a long time, and do not cease the treatment after the cautery; healing will hasten, and the two intentions will come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the abdomen should be a claw as we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is shown here.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in hydrophobia and filled with yellow water, you should cauterize between the little toe and ring finger on the bottom of the foot; raise your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, thus pressing against the yellow awl, and let the cautery follow this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After make 2 cauteries on each leg at the tip of the tibia; and let the cautery be long, one below the knee in front and the other above, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries in place for a long time without curing, until the water comes out; then cure the others that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When a belly ache comes from chill and moisture, the retentive and digestive virtue which is in the stomach and intestines becomes slackened, and cannot be cured by methods of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly with much strength, then do this: make one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of before regarding the cautery of the stomach, and make the cautery circulate; and around the belly make four small cauteries with a slender cautery needle, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, make cauteries on the shoulder, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and are old and consist of thick, cold, moist corruption, and have been treated as described in the section on division, but to no avail, then do cautery: III above the spine of the back, that which is completely removed below the diaper by poking gently and triangulating; perform cautery below the navel II times; and if you think the stomach is cold and the meat is not digesting, and one sees swelling in the face, then do a large cautery on the stomach as described earlier, and another on the liver, and another on the mouse with the entire cautery clove; and let the cautery remain open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating the area until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is named "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut into the thelul, heat the cautery which is like  .i. razor, and then put it all heated on that thelul cut; and keep your hand so that the cauteries reach the base of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of thelul, cauterize each one as we have said. After cure the area with beneficial ointments until it is healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the armpit, it will provide greater relief.
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, then such a disease comes that it cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is an ulcer and it is discharged and suppurates with pus and corrupt moisture, then you should probe it with a thin rod and take care to find out the depth of the ulcer all around.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	Then heat the cautery as a razor, and insert it into the ulcer according to the amount that the probe entered, and repeat the cautery until the pus and corruption are burned, once or twice or three times, according to the amount needed; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	if the ulcer goes to the bladder and intestines, then be careful of these places, and do not make the fire too strong, and think that it is not sensitive; after healing the area until it is healed, and if the place is swollen, and the matter is discharged for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed; and if the matter is not discharged, know that the place is pierced, and the bone at the bottom is corrupted; and thus as one of those which we will say in their place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes with rain and strong winds, and it does not subside with a woman's touch, then you must apply cautery to both sides of the rain with a hot iron as we have previously described; if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, which will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, and the patient retains urine, then you must apply cautery to the area above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic hair begin, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the nail of a thumb; and you should also apply 1 cautery below the back, or 2 if necessary; and the cauteries should be performed with the hot iron as described earlier.
de la marris	of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the wound is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their termini tardy; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore it is necessary that one be made .iij. cauteries around the wound, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and .ii. cauteries behind the back; and let the cauteries be claviate, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistors descend to the box of the hip, and because of this they move out of their place, and the sign is that one thigh is longer than the other when one measures them together; and it is found that the places of the division are hollow, then you must cauterize the patient on the box of the hip with 1 cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the place all around the box as it turns, so that the box is within the circle; and let the cautery be such as those with which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present to you, then make .iiij. cauteries of the olive oil large, and let the cautery be as deep as all the scabs; and cure it until it is healed.Et se tu veis ke li malaide ne se cure pas si grantment, si covient que tu le cauterizes sus la boiste de la hainche a  .iij. cauteres grans de l’olivaire, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the socket of the hip, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the disease is cured by what we have said in the division, but the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the disease of the gross humors with foul-smelling pills, or other good-smelling pills similar.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the wound has healed, you must cauterize it. There are two methods of cauterization: using burning medicines or fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery has many methods, one of which is as follows: cauterize the hip bone in three triangular cauteries according to this shape, making them deep and wide, with a space between each cautery the width of a thumb. Sometimes a cautery is made in the middle of the hip bone, so there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you want, cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have already said about the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the whole hip, and all the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is how it's done in sciatica, when the pain is in the hip and doesn't reach the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it extends to the thigh and leg, two cauteries are made where the patient feels the pain, and one cautery three inches above the ankle on the left side; the cautery should be cutaneous, burning through the thickness of the skin. And if the patient feels the pain extending to one or both feet, three cauteries are made, called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, make more cauteries; and if he feels that the pain is below the knee toward the thigh, then use a scalpel or circular cautery, and be careful in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery on so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who had cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they left it so that the leg was completely swollen, and the foot too, and it was pierced and corrupted all over the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a stomach ache from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two places together, do cautery in one and the other, according to this manner.Et se li dolours sont en deux partiés ensamble, fais cautère en l'une et en l'auter, selonc cette manière.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said about the cautery of the hip, that this is how it should be done: make the iron and let it be at the tip as large as a thumb nail, or a little less, and let it be pierced with holes and let there be spaces between them of the distance of the width of a thumb nail; and let there be bumps on both sides, and also like knobs, and let there be a handle well made; and this is its form:Et li sages dirent de la cauterie de la hainche, que ceste est la maniere: fai tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l'un entrechetre just a l'autre d'espaice la quantite d'un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi come noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c'est li forme:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it should be heated until it is all red and dripping, and then put it on the box of the painful hip, and twist it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery and leave it for three days; and then make an ointment of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the cure of anointing until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of its fearsome appearance, and few can endure it; and yet it is one of the good cauteries, which can be endured by those who know how to apply it.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The medicine cautery burns if you make the instrument to interlace so that the edge of the door descends, and it is made of brass or iron with a long surface, and in the thickness it has 2 nails, and between each one there is the quantity of the thickness of a fingernail; and they are open beneath and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Afterwards place the box of the hip on the patient lying on his healthy side, and press your hand hard on the box of the hip; afterwards pour between the two circles of the hot wax which is heated in the fire a little, and let the patient bear the heat and burning of it for an hour.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is as if it were bitten by fire; and when the bites are passed, take your hand with the instrument and raise the hip gently, and leave it thus for 3 days, and apply butter until what is black from the scald is removed; and let it be for 3 days so that pus comes out; and this would be the final aid after the treatment of ointments as far as he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or leg, you shall make the instrument that colors awe according to how you did in the hip joint; and that is the way of hot awe, and I have written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of each, and grind them together and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	In that pot with the small hole so that the point of a needle can enter; and place on top of this pot another pot well plugged, and put on top of the alkali and chalk and pour the gentle awe on top, as much as you have previously moistened it with your hand; and leave it so until there descends awe water and pieces into the plugged pot, then take all that awe, and pour it over the chalk and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then there will be much pain and it is treated with many remedies of medicine and with cauteries of other members, for it does evil work like fire, and also with other medicines such as theriac and honey and aniseed with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells of a cure where a man was healed from the pain in his hip and sciatic nerve, and he praised it highly, saying that no other treatment was used, and that the man was healed with just this one application, and afterwards he bathed as instructed below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he instructed how to apply litarge, green and dry, ground with a little fat, and place it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and leave it for three hours; and with the amount that the patient no longer feels the burn, then remove it.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter the bath until his body is a little warmed up, and let him enter the bed, and the pain will all leave and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery with such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it helps a lot; and the cautery must be performed in such a way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lamb's wool and grease it with old oil, and place it on the hollow between the big toe of the foot and the one next to it, which is called the 'foscile'.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that, take dry goat's dung and heat it in fire until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the lamb's wool, and let it remain there until it turns black; and do this again, and keep doing this until you feel through your sense that it reaches the hip and the pain ceases; and this type of cautery is called 'goat cautery'.
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes in the back, whether from sitting or a blow or from excessive evacuation, or by appearance of cold matter spread out, in none of these appearances is cautery useful except in that which comes from diffusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After the patient has been purged of foul pills or other means, you should make three lines on his back where the pain is located, and in each line .v. cauteries or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cautery should be performed according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see fit, do .iij. cauteries or .iiij. with the medium cautery clavis according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often afflicts small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight and painful buttock when they wake up, and fear; and you will find it in the lower spine of the back and in the appearance which comes over the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it being cured, then cauterize it with the cautery of celcle according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the purple cautery affects each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery tool, two or three lines in distance, and have the points close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterwards, heal the area until it is healthy according to what we have said, and be wary of administering cautery in a swollen area that is on a nerve ganglion.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of the joints is due to moistors that are spread throughout the body's members, and when the pain is in the feet, which the doctors properly call «podagra», and when it is caused by coldness and cannot be cured by medicine, then it is cured by cauterization in such a way: make the mark of cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-colored according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a need to prick near the base of the foot, do cautery with all the tool that is called «point».
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, do cautery on each knee three or four times with all the olive-sized cautery tool; and if you need more, then do more, but don't hold your hand in place any longer than until the skin is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, administer the cautery that we mentioned in his chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make a point around the wrist two lines; and if there is no more pain in the arms, make a point on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good treatment to the patient and take medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	Because if you give him good treatment and cleanse the phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rot of the eye socket
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rut comes in warts, and the bowels descend to the anus and it is new, then when you see him being treated, he must not eat anything that day; and he should use things that loosen the belly so that the farts descend from his belly; after that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the warts are repaired, and bring them up to your fingers, and sign with oil under the rut on the bone of the wrist, and all over a sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery from which this form comes:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and bleeding.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then realign the bones in their place; and have him hold his hand up so that they do not return; and work the thighs for the patient, and put a cushion and a sergeant under the thighs, and another under the foot which holds the hands; then put the cautery on the wound all over your palm, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the wound does not leak when you do the cautery, so that you do not burn yourself or the patient dies, or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cautery for children should be subtle according to the size of their ears, and for large people it should be large according to their size; after three days cure the site of the cautery with butter until the scald is healed; then treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well closed; and their clothing should be loose enough that they do not chafe when they move around in their rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, if a well-made bandage is applied and worn for another 40 days, and he keeps good rest, eats and drinks little, and avoids excessive exertion; then when he follows these instructions, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say next about the treatment of cutting on his shoulder.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly:
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they are not growing anymore, do cautery with the cautery depending on its quantity, and burn the third of the skin; after the cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it must be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the place of entry and make a line through the width above the ulcer, and another below, and hold your hand steady throughout the entire cautery process.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in a limb, whether from falling or injury, and the pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "point," and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb, its smallness and weakness, and its twisting and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, do another cautery on top of it, for usually it will move to the member nearest to it, so you should do cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of bleeding
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Sometimes diseases are cured by cautery with great difficulty, especially those that come from putrefaction of blood and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see it needs cauterization, take care whether the disease is in its beginning or not, and if it is cured according to what we have said before, without any ulceration or swelling, and you doubt that corruption might spread throughout the disease, then do five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head, and two at the front by the temples, and two behind on the nape of the neck; and hold your hand so that the cautery comes down to the bone, and vaporize the strong humors until they issue out; and cauterize the face according to what has been said.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the malady is scattered everywhere and is manifestly improving, then you should cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery in the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large cautery on the croup and another nearby, and two cauteries on each shoulder; and two cauteries on the elbows, and two cauteries on the tendons of the feet, and one cautery on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the back of the calf so that you do not burn them; and sometimes make one cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you do of cautery, the more you help it, and move it to profit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as the healthy do, because the body is already all corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterwards cure the place with wheat flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then make cauteries on the member according to its size; let the cautery be a little hot into the thickness of the skin; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cautery is done on the hand and foot and back, at the outlet of a nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus if the swelling is removed; and nevertheless no one should attempt this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the outlets of the nerves moving through the body.
de albaras	of poplars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" occurs, and medicine does not help, then cauterize it with a moderately deep cautery tool according to the thickness of the skin, until the white color is removed and the color changes; then treat it with a poultice of wheat flour and lentils, mixed with rose oil, plantain leaves, colon blood, and almond blood, each ingredient in equal parts. Mix everything together and apply it to the affected area, keeping it in place until the wound heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre first appears, and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is shaped like a circle, all around the edge of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nevertheless the wise say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; and nevertheless this does not seem good to me, for I fear it may be ulcerated and damaged, and I have indeed seen this happen sometimes; and a more certain thing is that it be cauterized around the edge, with the cautery called 'circle', as we have said about many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it is slow to die, either because of the excess fluid it produces or because of the age of the illness when it becomes decrepit (that is, very old), and there is little blood, or because of the time; and you see it hastening to die: therefore cauterize it all around with many small cauteries, piercing; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce through to the cautery, then heat the cautery with which this is formed:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced the skin, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them driving out in such a way that the course of the pustules is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, treat it until it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another type of disease which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a eating away of a limb, for it gnaws at the limbs just as fire burns dry wood.Et s’il corrodent les os, et li malaide est mortel; il doit estre treffuz par le meisme cauter, come susdis.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can withstand cautery with fire, then heat the cautery-irons small and large, according to what is suitable for the place where the disease is; after cauterizing it all over, so that you reach all the corruption, and none of it remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and put on the cauterized places a poultice with oil until the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of ointments that cause wounds to heal.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, then recommence the cautery on what remains of the diseased places.Si li membres sont treschiers, si covient que l’on les depeile, et adés le cure avec oignemens qui ont vertus ad curant char; et si ceu non, si covient qu’il soit osté, s’il ne peut demorer, par cautere de feu ou d’aultre maniere.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this swelling has sometimes been cured by a medicine poultice instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of much greater help, and I have already described the cure for a poultice in the division: take it whenever you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of warts that appear on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that through the feet there arises a disease which is called a 'clot' according to our understanding, and is a large hardened lump which blocks the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	Namely, fire cautery and hot water cautery.Et li fuels que on doit averir por ceste maladie, sont ainsis: pren sel, et vin, et oile, et poudres fin, et poivre, et gales, et terron de fer, et frens de cerf, et frens de renard, et frens de lonc best, et frens de lion, et frens de lonc pis, et frens de lonc peche, et frens d’ours, et frens de lonc chien, et frens de lonc chat; et prene tout ceste fuellie et mets a l’enverzun, et trais li pies et li solz, et li cotes de l’enverzun, et li costes de l’enverzun, et li tores de l’enverzun; et li cauteres que tu faras en li pies et en li solz et en li cotes et en li costes, et en li tores, doit averir selonc la guisance del pied qui est mal, si le pied est tort ou droit.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery, heat the cautery as hot as a feather of an owl, and made of good iron to the measure that it can touch the nail all around, and that it has thin edges; after, put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; leave it thus for three days until it begins to produce pus; then make a poultice of crushed mallows with salt, and leave the poultice all night, and the nail will fall off and be rooted out from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the place with ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by spreading throughout the body, and many times they occur in hands and feet, then you must administer hot-water cautery; and it is in such a way: take an iron or bronze rod, or an owl feather, and put it on the nail and the wart, that is to say, warts; and place the rod so that it presses all around, then put a little hot water, and hold your hand firmly and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the rod reaches the root of the nail, and can find the hot water a deep path right to the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will be uprooted at all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you extract all those in the body; then treat the wounds that generate pus with ointments.
li cure dou trembler	the cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble from the coldness of nerves, or from quartan fever or other, then you must make 4 cauteries or 4 on the spine, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach with olive cautery; then it will leave the trembling, and hasten the health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes sores appear on the surface of the body, or pustules that emit a foul odor, which come from corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If necessary, when they first appear, one should make a cautery on the top of each pustule: with a thin cautery of myrtle wood, whose point is taken up in fire, or with a long root of aristologe, or with a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning as they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow from that point forward, but the surplus matter from which they come is disrupted, and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.Et aucune fois il covient que li cauteres soit fait a la fin quan le puss est venuz et ne puet croistre en avant: selonc cest maniere qu’un cuit oignon, ou raifne, ou vergeile, ou fust de sauge, ou racine d’aristologe longue, ou fust de mirte subtil, ou cautere lenticulaire; et les met a leu que li puss soit venuz.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from outside, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grieving thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to anyone, you should quickly put your index finger over the wound of the vein, and press it hard until the blood is stopped beneath your finger, and no drops come out; then heat the olive-oil cautery rods, both small and large, until they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and the location where the artery is running, and place the cautery on that vein where you are holding your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bleeds again when you lift your finger from the wound and the cautery goes out, quickly take another of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and be careful that you don't hurt the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well stopped by itself if the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods we have mentioned: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by a strong ligature, or by medicines put on that have the power to stop bleeding; and it should be bound and compressed skillfully.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	He who attempts to stop the bleeding by tying it tightly with cloth or putting hot things on it, or similar things, will not help if he does not know how.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they do not have any medicine present, then they should put their index finger on the wound as we have said, and apply firm pressure until it is stopped up above the wound; and they should not move the finger but moisten it with cold water often so that it is very cold until the blood congeals, swells, and stops. And they should send someone to get what they need for cauteries and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all the diseases that require cauterization with fire or burning medicines, and the humors, causes, instruments, forms of cauteries; and I will go through this chapter along the same path so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauteries, and therefore greater caution is needed.Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to attempt foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from such who are so affected by their illness that they will die easily due to the foolishness they display in their sickness, and because of the great severity of their illness, one must be cautious with them.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you their sense and say, "Wait, I am healed"; and the illness is stubborn.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not consent to those who come to you with this manner, but place greater trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not open foolishly but wisely what you are certain of and can be proven and from which you can gain profit; and use prognostication and indication in curing your illnesses for which salvation is sought. And that will help you attain a good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may Our Lord grant you wisdom and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter in discussing by chapters, according to what is before the chapter of cauteries, which I have discussed from the head until the feet, so that you find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Do you know that this disease often comes to children when they are born, and when the umbilical cord is tightened too tightly around the child's neck; and sometimes it comes from a reason unknown to us.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen, death has always been the outcome; and because of this, it seems better to me to leave the treatment as it is.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw .I child whose shoulder was filled with water, and the head swelled every day until it could no longer support it; and he believed so much in moisture that he died, and this moisture is gathered under the bone above the diaphragm, between the heart and the bone; and the operations are such that when the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you split an opening in the head as wide as possible; and it should be as long as two fingers, until the moisture flows out; and see the shape of spatomile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the abscess is larger, then make two slits in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the edges of the head open on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and it has not closed up for you: then you must split an opening in the head according to this method:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all moisture fiercely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After the incisions, open the folds of skin and use powders, then apply wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then dislodge it, and treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head be extracted equally, and give the patient dry meat to eat, as much as the limb can bear, until the member is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at the size of the abscess and the gathering of the water; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut therefore where the abscess opens, and fill the gathering of water, and do it according to what you are able; and be careful not to cut the artery; and let blood flow, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	from gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone to have a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or feet, and the disease is old, and the medical cure does not help, then the last cure is cauterization with which one will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them covered, let the patient bend his head backward; then rub the area around a tough fold of skin until the arteries appear, then constrict the patient's neck with all his might while holding the skin taut; then examine where the vein drips, and the openings on either side are after the ears, and the pouches are pulled back; then sign the openings inside, then cover both with a pointed spatulum in two parts, as far as the jawbone, and it should be broad at the front of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, insert the spatulum under the artery and cover it from above, cutting as deep as two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is uncovered, let the blood flow upward continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feeling, then you must measure the quantity of the space of three digits, then cut deeply and slice up to the bone; and what amount of blood is appropriate to pour out is six parts, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then examine the wound: if nothing remains on the bone, no suppuration, then drain the wound and ligature it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	to migrate
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old inflammation comes, and a catarrh develops, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and ancient forensics and similar things, and it is treated by methods of medicine but none of it helps him, then we should extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extraction is that the patient should grow a beard on his temples, and feel for the artery which opens in the temple, as it opens noticeably by its beating, and is less reponsive to pressure in some people who are too cold; and if it is responsive, he should hold the artery with some cloth, then rub the area with some rough cloth, and moisten the area with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatulum of which there is a description below:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then draw it up with pincers, and separate it well from the tissues that are underneath in each part; and if the artery is тонкая, then return it to the tip of the fingernail, then ligature that part according to the quantity of two digits.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if she is not cut, her womb will not be clean all over.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from the vein until it is 1/6th full, up to 1/3rd; and if the artery is large, then tie it with a strong double silk thread in two places so that pus does not enter before the wound heals, and let the blood flow out freely; then cut away the excess between the two ligatures in the same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a hot iron until the bone is exposed; and this is the primary treatment if the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery aids in drying up moisture, therefore it is particularly helpful for wet sores.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And for the extraction of veins, one should fill the wound with old cotton and place it under well-made tents; and when they are removed, they should be treated with dry medicines that cause scabs to form, and with tents until they are healed; and if without cutting through the artery as much as you work on it, then hasten to cover it by cauterizing, or you can employ vitriolic ointment and press it in your hand so that the heat is drawn out of the vein; and if you do not have that present, then apply your finger to the site until the heat ceases, and moisten the site with cold water so that the heat stops, and press it as necessary; and what is better and lighter for the extraction of veins is to cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery of 2 parts, but the cutting edge should be well-spaced to retain its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when an instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less well.
