Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a thickness of one digit, and then when you have seared both sides and place the hot iron on until it reaches the bone, and open the vein in two places; and they should be spaced apart between the two shoulders because they are not welded together by this cautery all around; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	teardrops
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears fall from the eyes that are above the testicle on the head, and medicine does not help, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel in the forehead a pulsation like trembling; and if the eyes are sunken and moist so that the hair of the eyelids has fallen out, and the eyelids are burned and scalded by the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the old ones called it "cure contused", and you should do to the patient who has this disease the hairs on his forehead, then make III incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as long as two beans all over the forehead from top to bottom, and the other two on either side above the eyebrows, and beware of cutting the arteries that are on either side above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and each wound should be the size of three beans across the joint; and have a piece of sponge and a lot of cloth ready to soak up the blood, then put the spatumile in at both ends where the shape is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision at the temple all the way to the second incision; then scrape all around the skull between the two cuts up to the skin on top of the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second cut, and then remove this spathumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put into the first cut the instrument called "culter," which is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other, it is this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And cut along the coast towards the chest to the heart, and the under coast towards the bone, and slice it until it reaches the middle slit.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And tie all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to what opens from the heart, and then make another cut in the middle slit to the other defiant; then draw out blood equally, and express the place for the taken blood; then put a tent made of old cotton into each slit, and place wet clothes soaked in wine and oil and garlic on top, and be careful that no abscesses come to it; then on the third day loosen the bandage, and administer a lot of water with a sponge, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rosemary oil, and other remedies for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the eye

Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses. de l’estoupement des oreilles	the cleaning of the ears

de la gresle	of hail

then make a spatumile all along the two lines that you have signed, and start from the large nostril up to the small; and let one of the slits be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a hair root, then put the awl into one of the two angles of the heart, then scrape it all; then sew the two lips together with a thread of fine wool through an needle, and draw out the blood, and dry up the superfluity of the threads on the two nostrils with anything sticky if you see fit to do so; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the sewing and the threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without sewing it with dry and constricting things, for the paper revives at the souding of the wound and its joining, but the sewing is painful (as the ancients say), and this work is done without fear; and there is another way: and that is to mark the paper in a shape like the leaf of a myrtle, as we have described, with three points spread out according to the form which is shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above with small scissors evenly according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tweezers, and the object is not equal, then take a needle where there is a thread, and put it in the middle of the figure; and put another thread next to the large eyelid, and the second thread next to the small one, and bring the threads together equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above which you have marked, as we have described, then bring the two lips of the wound together by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerot and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes the hairs on the paper are converted: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the sewing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the cane is as follows: you should turn the paper and put it inside according to what I have said, then make .ij. canes by art, and .ij. subtle bonds as long as the paper and the width of the spatumile; and attach .ij. heads from .ij. parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above what is on top of the paper of the eye, and strain the .ij. canes from the .ij. formed parts; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that was strained will die and shrivel up and peel off as it falls away from itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed and the wound has force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up and the paper is lifted, the hairs will not grow anymore; and this is the form of the two cannas that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the works are such that you pierce a fine needle, and thread it with a soft and subtle silk thread; then assemble the heads and knot them subtly, and the length of the threads should be a palm long; then arrange in the case another fine silk thread, and knot the head of the thread; then place the patient's head in your hand; and have this in the sun so that the works are declared, for these are subtle and fine works, then thread the needle all the way into the paper until it reaches the hair root, and draw it up through the paper until it is completely drawn out; then draw your hand away so that the hairs come out straight with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the wound is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you will treat the wound underneath to the full extent that you have ordered, until the wound comes out from the opening above and you see it with your eye; then you will treat the wound and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for 1 or 2 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, accompany one long hair of the natural hairs, and let it grow with that one which you left, until it lengthens, then you will pull it out.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pustule of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or warts comes in the eye, there are two ways it can happen: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to treat it is to split the wart, and separate its lips, and place inside tents of linen, and leave it until it heals; and you must not use in its treatment anything that dries and constricts.Et si tu ne puis desanier li, si covient que tu le fendes et laves en l’eau chaude, et metes dedens tenture de lin, et laves le de nouveau, et tant fais jusques qu’il soit sanee.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And if you cannot heal it, then you should split and wash it in warm water, and place a linen tent over it, and wash it again, and do this until it is healed.For if you use dry things, the disease will return worse than before; but use softening things like fenugreek, and rosewater or altée and flaxseed cooked in oil, and apply an ointment of roasted linseed, and wrap it up in a tent, and treat it thus.Et si le maladie vient en la paupiere, si covient que tu metes dedins une tente de lin, et tu la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; mais ne fas pas en li tenture de lin qui soit cuit en aigue chaude, car il adoublet li maladie.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must be careful that it does not heal according to the shape it was before; and these works that we have said are not remedies for this disease, but treatments so that it does not return to the shape it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is underneath, which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidents come from wounds and incisions and cauterizations and similar things; and the way to treat them is that you take a needle with a double thread, and pierce it into the flesh, and make it pass through from the left armpit so that the thread comes out in two places on the chest; then the flesh above is sutured all around the needle, and the knot is tied at the broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the wound returns as it should be, that is good; if not, then take a razor and put it in the incision, and turn the flesh, and make two incisions along the sides inside the flesh; and the ends of the two incisions should be at the two angles of the incision you have sewed up, so that when they are brought together, the shape is like the shape of a letter which has the name  "I Greek"; then remove this flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are torn beneath it, from what follows the flesh, then join the two torn parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it as we have said with softening medicines and poultices, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the malady comes from a split or sewing or cautery, then you must make a plain split under the hair of the scalp, and according to what is mentioned above; then unscrew between the two lips of the tent, as I have said; and one should perform the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares devices with all his power so that he causes the figure to return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what they require of operation and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the scalp
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suddenness happens to humans in such a way that the scalp is separated from the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must stick the tip of a razor under the scalp and lift it upward; and use tweezers, so that you grasp what is cut by the spatula, which is neither too blunt nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot bear to have the eye too deeply cut; and make your incision, by which you peel off this union, gently, so that the scalp returns according to its natural form; and all of this union is healed, and sometimes in the eye there is a saline discharge, and it is relieved with warm water and a bandage; then place between the scalp and the eye a tent made of linen, and place over the eye a damp piece of wool; and after three days, use the ointment and the soothing remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You should know that the nail has two forms: one is nerveous and resembles a tough membrane; the other is not nerveous but resembles congealed white moisture, such that when you touch it with iron and try to cut it with pincers, nothing happens. Both types originate from the inner corner of the eye, and grow little by little until they cover the entire sight and light, and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of the incision is that the patient should turn his head towards you, then open their eyes; and hold the paper in your hand, then grab the nail with pincers of small pliers, and stab it at the top; then take a needle, and insert a horsehair, or cow's hair, or ox's hair, and a strong thread; and double over the tip of the needle a little and push it into the nail, and tie the nail to the thread and stab it at the top, and scrape along the side of the nail that follows the eyelid and the eye until the end of the lash, then cut the rest in the root of the tear duct with great care and small forces, leaving the natural membrane of the tear duct untouched; and sometimes only stab the nail at the edge of the eyelid, and the thread, as we have said. Then scrape it along the entire tear sac carefully:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the tear sac does not touch the fleshy membrane and tear it, and that the eyelid is not pierced; after the incision, apply a little powdered quicklime to the eye, and make a collar out of it, and leave it on until the next day; then clean the eye as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the nail is not sensitive, and you cannot push in the needle, and the hook does not fit inside it, many times this kind of nail is cured with medicine; they grow as I have described in the division, and if you see that it covers up, then treat the eye of the patient, and take a light spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently, and if you see that it does not shrink and the pus is still coming out, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red copper and sea salt ground up, and swab the eye until the next day; then start the other treatment again according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then start the treatment again as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid is harmful to the eye in a great way, then suspend it on the hook, and cut off a part but not all of it so that the body of tears does not come; then distill into the eye a red collar made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the eye which grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men, a red lump sometimes appears on the eyelid, covering the pupil and pressing against the eyelids, resembling a rose on a baluster; the patient then puts their head down, and they work on the eye, and they push all this flesh towards the nails, suitable for this purpose, and hold it there with force; then they cut through the first lump of flesh, and continue cutting all the way to the eyeball, taking care not to blink during the operation; and the incision should be made as described in the section on nail incisions, using gentle pressure to remove the membrane, as demonstrated in this chapter; once the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, apply a mixture of crushed vitriol or similar corrosive medicines to the eye, and place cotton soaked in egg white over it to protect against hot abscesses; if anything remains, and the white turns red, indicating a hot abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with cooling remedies; then return to the operation once the eye has healed, and repeat this process for each lump of flesh that appears in the eye.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you must use caution when treating weak eyes with the natural method or accidentally with iron; and do not force your hand in any of these treatments until you see that the patient is suffering from this procedure.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins cover the eyes, hindering vision and weakening the eyes every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first examine the eyes to see if there is any other disease besides the red veins; then treat them in this way: instruct the patient to lean his head back, then squeeze those veins gently all around according to your wisdom, and make the incisions on the eyelids subtle and double according to this shape.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And two incisions in .i. body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then squeeze those veins gently, and let the blood out an hour after another, until you see the veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to damage the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very careful in your work so that you do not touch anything but the veins; and when you have done that, then distill into the eye green and red koliri to corrupt what is left of the stye.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot pull out all of this in that hour, then make a plaster over the eye from things that soothe the pain of them, and let it be for several days until the pain is eased and the hot abscess is assured, then start again according to this way which is before, until he is healed; and this is the form of strength:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Examine the fistula closely: when you heal it with cautery and medicine that burns according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then dig into the abscess where it should be, and draw out all the moisture from it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you will see the corruption and blackness, then it returns to all its instruments from which this form comes; and it is called a "harsh head", and should be made into a .i. sharp point, and punctured like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand slightly until you know that the corruption is gone; and do this several times, then restore the site with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the vein is glued and the body of the bow is glued and remains that way for 40 days without becoming inflamed and nothing bad happens, then you know it is healed; if not, there is only one other thing to do, which is to open the fistula at the opening of the nostril according to this shape: and you must uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take out the forest according to this shape, and the head of the tool should have three angles, and the shaft should be tapered to a point as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then places it on the bone of the eye socket, and moves his hand away from the eye a little, then returns to the entire socket until he pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the vent in his finger if he holds his hand over his nose; then restore the area with dry medicine as I have taught you, and when the flesh heals and hardens, test the matter on the nose; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye's output
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open and there is no disturbance to the brain or eye damage, you should bind the patient; then cleanse the eye, then apply leeches or suck out the fluid without piercing, then place on the eye a poultice made of acacia gum, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla; then tightly bind the eye with bandages and cloth, the cloth being folded in half four times to create several layers, and then placed one on top of the other according to how much the eye needs; then tightly bind it from above with a firm bandage, and repeat the leeches to suck out the fluid without piercing; then remove the leeches and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the poultice softens, you should tightly bind it again; then remove the poultice after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, repeat the poultice and bandages until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the rupture of a woven veil
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a tear occurs in woven fabric, it opens and appears like a grain of resin, and is terrifying to look at. Therefore, if you see it breaking, the work is such that you should pierce the fabric with a needle at the root of the tear from the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread in the edge of the tear; and pierce the fabric, and leave the first needle according to its position. Then, tie the double thread around the tear and tightly bind it, then remove the needle and place a soft pad moistened with egg white over the eye, and leave it until the threads cut through the veil, then cleanse the eye with comforting substances until it is healed. Sometimes, the tear is constrained by a circle of cloth on each side until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great appearance, then pierce them with a spatumile needle which comes from the bottom of the eye, and remove the white moist film and bring down the eyes, and enter immediately thereafter; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, which is called "alcunnati", is nothing but a swelling gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the treatment is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then take his head between your hands and move it until you see the swelling come to your eyes; then it should be pinched, and the light should be blocked, and the patient should see things as he used to; and if it does not go down below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not apparent as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the spatula and cut through the corneum to the conjunctiva, and as far as the bowels; and when it is issued, let hot water infused with honey, or water in which fenugreek and honey have been boiled, be distilled into the eye, and then let it be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have described the appearances of diseases in the division, and what should be done to pierce them; now act according to the instructions given.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and close and squeeze his healthy eye tightly; then place the paper over his affected eye, with the right side of the paper over a right eye, or the left side over a left eye; then take in your right hand, if it is a right eye, the instrument called «almagda», or in your left hand if it is a left eye; then put the tip of the instrument next to the cornea through the white part of the eye at the edge of the lower eyelid, and push the instrument called «almagda» skillfully, and twist your hand until it pierces the white part of the eye, and feel that «almagda» comes into contact with the empty space; and the depth of the «almagda» should be equal to the thickness of a plum from the edge of the black part to the end of the white part; this is the cornea of the eye; then you will see the bone through the paper because of the clarity of the cornea, and then push the instrument until it reaches the aqueous humor, then express it beneath one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water is flowing now, then the patient will see the instrument in front of him and the doctor's hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest for a little while, and if the water flows back the second way, push it out with the instrument, and when it is stuck in and not flowing up, gently twist your hand a bit; then put some more gem-water into the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then insert the eye with cotton wool or lamb's wool soaked in rose oil and in plenty of egg white, and bind it up with clean cloth.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put on crushed comfrey with plenty of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if  'almagda' cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you should take the instrument called  'alberit', of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so, therefore, cut only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make the cut fine, then pour in the gem-water as we have said; and when the operation is complete, prepare for the patient a dark room to sleep in on his back in a dim place; and he must abstain from all movement, and eat light food, and not move his head or to the right or left, and he must be bound according to his condition for three days; then loosen him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the hour of the incision or now, but you must ease it so that the water flows gently.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If such an abscess comes, you must release the eye before the seventh day, and apply that which soothes abscesses; and when it is pacified, then release the eyelid and place over his face a gold rim to cover any eye, and let him be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then exit the house a little at a time, and return to his case; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Spain who told us that in his country they make a slit in the almighty, and suck out the water, but I have never seen this done in our land, nor have I ever read of it in ancient books; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of almandine, so that those who do not know them can see them; and they are properly made of bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the tops of the horns should be of the same subtlety, and the tips in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart through the chest
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes strange horses are born with various defects, some of which look like scorpions with many feet; and there are some with a hoofed leg of a good color, and there is a hoofed leg of a good color.Et il y a certaines qui sont nées avec une seule corne, et d'autres avec des cornes à l'arrière, et certaines avec des cornes comme des chèvres, et d'autres avec des cornes comme des béliers, et certaines avec des cornes comme des vaches, et d'autres avec des cornes comme des buffles, et certaines avec des cornes comme des licornes.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case, with these carts which are soft and not encrusted, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, pour wine on the carts, and pull them out; then hold what you can with a thin spatulate instrument from one side, until you know that the cart is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If any of the matter remains that we cannot cover, then open it up with one of the subtle instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if without it overwhelming you, or causing an abscess, then cut it out as it should be; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten to cauterize them until the blood is stanched and all the pus is removed, then pour on new wine and water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the ears open and moisture comes to the palate, you know that he is cured; and if moisture does not pass through as it should, you know that there is a cart in the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut out: therefore you must insert a thick thread of linen there, which has been soaked in water, and let it hang down by itself, with one end or the other sticking out; put the end of the thread into the patient's nostril as far as he can bear it, until you feel that the cart is entirely removed.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as long as you know that the nails have corrupted the flesh, then pull out the nail, wash the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the ear as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that is left of the flesh; and then put in the ear a plug of plaster for some days until it is healed, and if it needs dry medicines, then use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the ears.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	It should be made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the conduit as well; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be hollow for purging the nose; and it should have a handle at the end to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart through the chest
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the top of the chest, and grows and becomes large, until it is visible to the eye; and for this reason you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all the pus, then place the cautery or burning medicine on it; and if one delays cutting it until it has become large, then be wary whether it is hard, of a dark color, and lacking in feeling: do not touch it with iron, for this is an abscess, for when it is cut at any time, great harm comes to the patient. And if the abscess is due only to pressure, not from a dark color, and you see that one can completely cover it, then empty the wound and cut it without fear, and cure the place of dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the chest has been cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilages, it benefits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, whenever this happens to anyone, look to see if the wound is fresh and bleeding; then bring together the two lips of the wound with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are torn on both sides, then you must scrape away all the dead flesh from around the wound, then bring together the two lips with a stitch and hold them, and powder dragon's blood and incense together over them; and put a piece of strong plaster or other healing plaster over the powders, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either with needles as we have said in sewing the belly; or with thread, as I have made you understand.
des apostemes des levres	from abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, there are hard abscesses on the lips, similar to grains of wheat, both smaller and larger; therefore, you should turn over the lip, and cut above each pustule, and squeeze it with tweezers, and then apply vitriolated powder to the incision until the blood is staunched. Then use garlic and treat the area with dry substances until it heals.
de la char des gencives	from gum swelling
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth appears on the gums, which the elders call "albus". You should hold it with tongs and cut at its root, letting the blood or pus flow out; then place ground vitriol or other restraining and drying powders over the site. If the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; it will not return after cautery. These are the forms for treating growths.
des sordens	from disorders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the base of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, and there are ugly and rough growths; sometimes teeth are black, green, or yellow, so that corruption has reached the gums, and they stink; so you should have the patient hold his head in your hands and open his mouth wide, and examine the teeth where the growths appear, removing everything completely. And thus you will do with the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other discolourations, cleaning them all up. If you remove what is there at first, that is good; if not, then do it again the next day and the day after, until you have removed everything. Know that teeth require diverse forms of instruments for scraping, depending on what the work shows you, so that the tools used to scrape between teeth are different from those used to scrape the gums. And these forms and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a tooth for its pain, you should delay drawing it as long as possible, because one must not do that; for that is a very high substance up to the point that one has no excuse to pull it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is compelled to draw breath, you must be certain about the toothache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and believes it to be in a sound tooth, and has the healthy tooth pulled; and nevertheless the pain does not go away because of this, until the evil tooth is extracted, for we have often tried this with these doctors; and when you are quite certain about the toothache, you must scrape around the tooth all around, spitting strongly to push back the gum from all sides; then he moves it with his fingers or with fine tweezers, little by little, until it is well loosened, then he applies the tweezers firmly; and let the patient's head be between your knees, and hold it fast so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Afterwards, extract the tooth firmly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of those instruments and insert it into each side gently, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, you should fill the hole with linen, and gently constrict it with forceps so that it does not break while being extracted; and one must work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, leaving a part behind, which will cause greater pain due to the root's maliciousness.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware of doing as ignorant surgeons do, who in their haste and arrogance sometimes break a tooth, not heeding what we have instructed; they sometimes bring about great illness due to the roots remaining, or by breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, wash the socket with wine or garlic and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often does, apply powdered vitriol to the site; and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, which are mute to the teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not break when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of thick material so that they do not bend when pulling, and should be well-made iron, and should be toothed to hold the mucous.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the tract, you must place moistened cotton on it for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the skin softens, then use the forceps called 'algefri', which resemble a pair of tongs; inside they are serrated like a file and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with these tweezers, then you should uncover the skin all around the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", which is a spatula, whose shape is like this:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be firm and wide so that it does not break, and if the root comes out with this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, whose forms come after this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one should use this instrument which has two ends, whose shape is like this:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are in the reason of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tweezers, whose shape is like this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And have this instrument ready so that it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments for teeth; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise master finds his own instrument through his own skills, according to what his work and the disease show him, because there are many diseases for which the ancients did not teach an instrument due to their diversity. And if it does not break in the cart or other bones, but protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, as I have told you, and helps with gestures; this is how it is done:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting so as to hold the bone, so that it does not slip but can be held and removed; and then restore the site with appropriate medicines. And if there is protrusion in the bone, and it is small, then treat it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to nature and its shape is ugly, especially in young women, you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down; then pull it out. And if there is an air pocket with the tooth, take this instrument, of which there is a drawing, and it should resemble a small beak, and be made of tempered iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And push it gently into the gums for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it with a type of file as shown in the drawing:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file with which we make needles; and file the tooth a little bit each day gently, so that it does not move until it is straight; then smooth it at the end completely with any file, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file down the roughness so that it is even and doesn't cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is loose due to an injury or decay, and the patient cannot bite down on anything without pain, and you have treated them with constricting medicines without success, then they must be bound with a gold wire, as silver wire turns green and rusts, but gold never changes; the wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the size of the gap between the teeth. If you want to pull out the tooth, take the wire and wrap it around both healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth between the molars, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the binding process from the starting point, pulling your hand gently and firmly so that it does not move. The wire should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then clip the teeth with tweezers, and bring them together, and fit them between the healthy teeth, and put it in so that it does not bite the tongue; and then leave it tightly for as long as it can stay, and if it slips, or the wires break, then tighten it with another wire; let it remain and serve thus all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the healthy II teeth, and the II bad ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, if it is replaced in its place, fresh after fresh, as we have said; and only a wise and experienced person should attempt this. Sometimes, the shape of a tooth is made from cow bone, and placed where the deficiency is, then restrained as we have described, and remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the vein of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes the tongue is tied under the tongue by nature, which one is born with; or by accident from a wound; and the treatment is that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your healthy mouth, and loosen the tongue; then grab the nervous ligament widely so that the tongue is loosened from its socket, and if there is hardness or a nodule, and this is due to a wound, then he inserts the hook and grabs the ligament widely; and be careful that the split is not too deep for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, lift the place with rose water and garlic, or cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and dye the patient's tongue every night so that it does not stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, place powdered vitriol over the site; and if the blood stops, cauterize with a lentigo cautery, which is good for this. Then treat it further until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it discolored black or hard, and the patient does not feel any pain, then do not touch it because it is a ulcer; and if it is declining into a blister and there is moisture, cut into it with a spatulum, and free it from both sides; and if the bleeding starts at your action, apply crushed vitriol until it stops, then return to your action until you draw out everything; then raise the area with vinegar and salt, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there are sores in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "almonds". When treating them as we have described in the division, if they are not healed, take care: if there are hard sores of small size and a pale color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also to prevent bleeding; but leave it until it is mature, and then you will burst it, or it will break on its own. And if it is of a pale color and the root is thin, have the instrument ready to cover it, but first check that the sore is calm and soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore let the patient sit facing the sun, and his head should be in your shade, and he should open his mouth and the servant should hold the implement between his hands, and press the tongue underneath at its tip, where the shape is; it should be made of silver or thin brass, just like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Then you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the hook and insert it into the almond, and pull it out from above as much as you can; and draw some threads of the fabric along with it, then cover the instrument with which comes the form, resembling a needle; and even so the points are bent, one to the left and the other to the right, and they are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cover it with tweezers, from which comes the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it is sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, then cut the other according to the same method, and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water, and with vinegar and garlic, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water, or with pomegranate peels that have been cooked, or with bay leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them thus as you cut the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.
