And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and she had a very closed throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway which was blocked, and she could not eat or drink, and would have died if it continued like this for one or two more days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had become so swollen that it had forced its way out through both nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened therefore, and inserted a hook into one of the nostrils, then drew it out, and took out a large amount of pus; then I did the same in the other nostril, and opened up her mouth and pressed down on her tongue; afterwards, I inserted the hook into the abscess, and scooped out some of its contents, and only a little blood came out; thus the passageway in the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to lance this abscess for a long time; and it would shrink again and fill up the space that I had emptied, so that it became very large; therefore, I packed it with a poultice and cauterized it inside her throat; thus it did not grow any more; and I left those parts, and God alone knew what happened to her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eye descends to the socket, and it is swollen and long, it is called 'perpendicular'; and if it is thick and round below, it is called an 'eye'.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it has been drained as we have said in the division, and the drainage does not help, and you see that the abscess is calmed down, and it is thin, then you should cover it; and the one which is round and not long, and it is blood-red or of a dusky color, then you should avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it according to the manner which I have described, with its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue to the instrument of which we spoke earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it out, and cover it with one of the two instruments which I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut away more than the excess that is beyond the natural boundary; for if you cut away more, it damages the voice and speech. And after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two testicles, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you should use the cautery of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is for acute disease.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put his head against your sound shoulder, and then press his tongue against the instrument that we have described in the chapter on cautery, and heat it with live fire, so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and use the implement of which this is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and has a hair or thread to hold the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and puts the instrument into all the medicine on the iris; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth due to the medicine inside, so that it does not go down into the throat and lungs. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the iris for the duration of half an hour, until you see it hardening and the bites of the medicine calming down. If you see anything, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton all around the eye, so that the cotton adheres to the iris; do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry for 4 or 5 days. If you need to renew the cautery with more medicine, do so, and after the cautery, wash the area around the eye with cold water, and treat it with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this way, take calaminus and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and assemble all of them or some of them in one pot, and add vinegar, and let it boil. The pot should be well-glazed with strong earth, and the instrument inside should be cheved according to this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, and one end should be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eyeball is mortified; then he should do this often, until the eyeball dries out, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things can happen there; nor do this beyond the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a wooden stick and place an egg white on the tip, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the egg white will not allow the vapors to burden the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times there is stuck in the throat a bone or spine of a fish, or some other object; therefore you must pull out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you move the object; and if it does not appear to you and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will stick, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out in the way we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and let the end be lifted upwards; and beware of touching the epiglottis, lest he choke, nor push the bone inside; and move as long as the patient has to vomit, so that the object is dislodged; then he swallows it, or pulls it out with the whole instrument equally, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the bloodletting, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, and then press his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out a little bit at a time with a small hook or subtle tweezers suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a carved wooden stick and insert it into the throat of the patient, then place the heated end of the stick in the groove of the stick, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Take a full glass of cold water and open the mouth, pour it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; as soon as the blood feels the water, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not stop as we have said, then smoke out the patient with assafetida, using the instrument I described for smoking out the eye; do this many times, for it will stop without bleeding.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way to do the smoking is to put burning charcoal in a pot and cover it with a perforated lid, and place the instrument's tip in the hole; then pour in your smoke, and the patient should hold their breath with their head inside their mouth, closing their mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes directly to the blood; and the blood will stop now, and if it does not, repeat the smoking many times; and let the patient endure thirst, eating only salted and dry things, and drink nothing; and then they will surely pass away due to this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And if he needs to drink before the blood stops flowing, then let him drink warm wine or grape juice; for the blood will want to go to the stomach and be relaxed, and once it is there, the wine will take hold of it and draw it out.
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, depending on what the memory of one and another comes after in this book, and they differ in penetration and size; and there are two ways, one is in its appearance itself, and from what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is due to the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses in the head are different from those in the bottom, and the abscesses in the fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the boil is mature according to its fulfillment; and there are some that one must pierce when they become crushed, and they do not die according to their fulfillment, as with abscesses that are near joints. Car li bowe qui sont delez jointures ne doit mie estre percie tant que il ne soit meure, car li maux se part en la percier, et li maux qui il a avant la percier est grant; si com li apostemes qui vient sus la cheville qui leu tient la cheville.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from these joints and are left until they are rotten all around, the ligaments and nerves of the joint may be corrupted, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is near the principal limb and you delay piercing it until it is rotten, it will harm the principal limb. If it is near the anus, one should pierce it so that it may rot inside and be prolonged within, and a fistula may result; it may not heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And one should know the time of piercing the abscess that is mature according to its development, and that is when the pain subsides, and the decline of fever, and the lessening of pain and redness, and from the discharge and the sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and one should make the piercing where the abscess is most dependent, and where it appears there is pus. And the piercing should be made from the long side of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints affecting nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to let the piercing be until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body where the venom comes from will be prolonged, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and the depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that has been pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat small abscesses with small incisions; and large abscesses with large incisions, and many slits according to the appearance of their size; and in such abscesses where one must cut into the skin, and cover; when they have become as hard as a grape, and are deadened, one should do as one does with blisters: and there are some that are split into three angles, and some which one covers like the fruit of the myrtle, like abscesses in the intestines; and there are some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions, and similar covering.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, you must pierce it plainly; and when the abscess is large and has drawn a great boil, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the boil at once, but only a part; then stop the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again; do this several times from time to time, until the boil is completely drained; likewise if the patient is of feeble strength, or a woman carrying child, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus sometimes leaps out with the opening of the boil, and the patient might die from it without you realizing.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, handle this chapter with great caution; and when you have pierced the abscess, wash the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, apply tenters made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many openings, you should put a tenter in each one so that they touch; and if you have cut into the abscess at its edge, and spread it open, then you should fill it with old cotton or the shavings of linen without moisture, and leave it for three days; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs from your work, then apply cold water and ease it, and wet the cloth, and place it over the bleeding spot many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding continues, then apply treatment and care, and the powders that I have described with my own hands in this book; and if it is in the winter, and the area around the abscess is very nervous, then you should place wet tents and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil over it; and if it is in the summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should place wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or cool wine and oil, for a third of the day, as we have said; then open the abscess and wash and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And so it is necessary to know generally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should go about treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the head come small abscesses, and they are of our nature, like the pustules on a newborn infant's skin, and there are many similarities among them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are greasy and others where there is moisture like pus; and there are also hard and stony ones, and there is no doubt if the artery does not act against them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the stomach is such that you must test with every instrument called a "trocar", from which the forms come later, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they will release it from above through the long tube.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is released, they scrape it without leaving any of the skin that contains the moisture, for it returns later if nothing is left behind; then plunge cotton into Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain overnight will be cured.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the cotton again, as before, on the second and third day, until you know well that it does not stay at night; then cure the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains pus, then open it according to this form, from above; and pour out your fingers, and scrape off all of it, and put all of your treatment into drawing out the pus under the skin; and if the artery makes a sound contrary to you, then do what I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do for the abscess if it is deep, and cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cut on the deep abscess and the moist one is lighter, because they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or bumps have no moisture, and some were the abscesses that I described in a chief of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if anyone had cut them they would have made just as much of a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, apart from those that come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should be at the lowest most dependent location in order for pus to drain; and the treatment should be as it should be.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and they are large and intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own region, just as the scrofula and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similar scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malignant and do not want to heal.Et li scrophules sont maintes foiz en l’enditure des ossels, et en la cote dou col, et en la nuque, et en les asseles, et en la teste, et sous la racine des oreilles; et si contienent moistor et sang, et sont mout dolerues.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Therefore, when you see one that is well-disposed for cauterization and resembles the color of the body, and is mute in every part and not discolored by the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not deep; then you should cover it from above and scrape each part, and if necessary, cut the two lips of the heart with an incision, as we have said for head abscesses. Then draw it little by little, making sure that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, and avoid burning or trenchant so that the hand does not slip, and do not go too far forward, so that you do not cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cover the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, then put into the wound vitriol ground, or some powders that stop bleeding, and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to fester.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is healed, return to your work until you finish it; then examine with your finger if there are any small sores remaining, and scrape and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If there is a large vein at the root of the sore, you should not scrape that sore at its root but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall without causing harm; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment and heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you scrape the entire sore, you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now so that there is no superfluity remaining due to the size of the sore.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you should proceed to scrape its root and pull it out, then sew it as we have said.Quant la plaie est curiee, si covient que tu l’empraies de baume armoy, et li li gisunt par dessus, et le guarisist si com nos avons dit.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Scrofula that holds surplus pus, pierce there where it oozes; and pierce as above, depending on it, then administer poultices with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is left of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, then treat with an ointment poultice until it heals.
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the script of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squint, the slit in the throat called the 'epiglottis' should be cut; and one must not make an incision by this, because all the veins and the lung of the sick person are at those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the lungs, one must cover the epiglottis to prevent loss due to strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we should split it under three circles or four, a small split across, between the two circles, or by the amount of the split in the soft palate; and those places that are suitable for splitting the epiglottis where there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then he should extend the skin of the throat to the epiglottis, then split the cartilage until it reaches the uvula; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut the soft palate, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the splitting of the vein of the uvula, which flows out through the opening that is made, and by the failure of the voice; and leave the wound open a little.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and one no longer doubts about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the heart wound, and heal it completely without the cartilage; then administer medications that promote flesh growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely swollen and the patient is judged dead and the pulse has ceased.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And then they cut the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe through the wound and thus be guarded from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the maliciousness of the disease passed, which passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it until it healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stabbed herself in the throat, piercing part of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that the blood which had issued from it had not flowed further than the throat, and the windpipe was intact.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound and treated it until it healed; and the lady had no more trouble with her voice, and returned to her former state; therefore I say that one should not fear cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This hernia is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large hernia in color like jaundice, and it occurs often in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental; the natural type has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type occurs in two ways: one resembles a fatty tumor, and the other is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear of it, and one should not apply force unless it is small, and test and examine all the openings: if you find it just like fat tissue, and it cannot be pushed or moved in any way, then cut it open, as one would a cyst, and treat it thoroughly throughout its entire depth, if there is nothing inside; and examine carefully, and treat it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of doing this, all of which I will describe; but now I must explain the difference between a nosebleed and a hemorrhage.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is hot and feverish, as long as the effusion has not passed, and the swelling is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a nosebleed there is no heat, fever, or pain; and it contains phlegm, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a boil, and becomes swollen; and they are according to two appearances, either dry or moist, and many in color are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the eye, you should first test and examine it with the instrument called an "optical probe", according to what its shape will appear in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of inquiring into abscesses in the nose is that you press on the most moist spot that you find in the abscess, and twist your fingers slightly, until you feel that the pus has pierced the membrane; then, according to the size of the abscess, extract the instrument and be careful not to push too far.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the pus is thin and of any color, treat it as I have described for other abscesses; but if no pus comes after the incision, know that it is fatty, so cross it with a knife, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape each side, and guard the skin where it lies, that you draw it healthy with the needle; and if you cannot draw it healthy, then draw it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, it will come back many times; and if a little remains, and the wound is not painful to you, employ some corrosive powders on the wound, and press the wound, and apply hot healing poultices, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the boil is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with what produces scabs.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein underneath is contrary to you or another, then hasten and employ the place of vitriol ground, and leave it for two or three days until the wound suppurates and the ebullition of blood subsides; then return to cover what has been delayed by the night.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the trocar, which come in three varieties: large, medium, and small. There are also three types of handle: one called an "albaret", another a "breb", and a third with three variations: large, medium, and small, used to pierce abscesses and fistulas. They are similar to the needles used to sew up wounds and are made of brass, iron, or silver. The yellow ones are valued more highly and are often used with black thread to close fistula wounds. They come in three sizes depending on the size of the aperture.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the knives are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small. There are also knives with two curves that come in three varieties, as well as knives with three curves that come in three sizes. There are also knives with one curve only, which also come in three sizes, and all of these are necessary for their respective purposes.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are sharp, and there are some that do not cut beyond one side, with which we scorch the nose, so that we do not cut the vein or nerve; and by means of these probes, the veins are bound in wounds, so that the patient does not bleed when opening abscesses; and they come in three types: large, small, and medium, as you see; and we do not use them beyond fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes a small instrument resembling cuts of fingernails is made according to this form, with which blood is staunched:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is put sometimes in the place that heals by gathering veins, and sometimes according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell up when they become corrupt, so that they look like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and if anyone wants to cure them, it is necessary to bleed according to this form from b. to g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scorch the fat, and fill the wound with medicine, then bring together the two lips of the wound by suturing, and heal it until it is healthy; and if the nipple droops downward, and becomes soft because of its size as happens to women, then make two cuts above it in the shape of a V; so that one lip is attached to the other at the end of each cut, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form .b. up to the line .g.; then scorch the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about suturing and powders, and what is necessary for healing, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood flow, then you should fill the wound with wet cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it dissolves the remaining fat and flesh, then heal it until it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are like hard scrofula, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowels which are in the abscess have been emptied, employ the wound with soft cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, they should be treated as we have said for fissures of scrofula, and if the wound is closed, the cautery should be administered as mentioned earlier.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is open and the skin above it, this often leads to abscesses, and also causes swelling of the vein; and one can recognize this when it is due to the artery, as the abscesses are long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a pulling sensation; and when it is due to the vein, there is a red and swollen appearance; and it is foolish to cover this kind of abscess, especially when it is below the nipples and in the armpits, neck, and many other places, and it is severe.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore one must avoid cauterizing with iron, and if it is on the head, one must also avoid cauterizing there; and when it is swelling due to an artery, one should cut through the skin from above along its length, then open the artery widely from the artery-vein junction, and gently pull out the artery from its surrounding tissues until it is completely exposed; then insert a needle beneath the skin at one end of the aperture and pierce through to the other side, and draw the artery tightly with a double thread in two places according to how I taught you for the extraction of the two temporal arteries; then pierce the area between the two threads with an incision instrument so that the blood flows out which is inside, and draw out the abscess; then administer the cure that involves cauterizing with a red-hot iron, until the thread loosens; then cure it with appropriate ointments until it heals; and if the abscess is due to the vein, one should take some of the pus from the abscess with one's hand, then insert the needle below the skin where one is holding the hand, and pierce through to the other side, and draw a double thread through so that you can pull the artery tightly in three places; then cut off the superfluous skin from around the abscess, then cut away the superfluous skin of the wound, leaving only what is tied with the thread; then place a moistened cloth in wine and oil over it, then administer treatments with tenting and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come to the artery and vein, they come to the nerves when they are injured, or from too much exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens most often in the shoulders and elbows, and all over where there are joints, and it is called an aposteme, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various states without pain; and when one applies pressure to it, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body but beneath the skin; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, or downward or upward, and that which is in joints should not be covered with iron: lest there be contraction; and for that which is on the head or forehead, use a spatumile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the aposteme is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a hook, then scrape off the skin, cut out the bone, and close the wound with stitches, healing it until it is cured.
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There are times when it occurs in the stomach and nowhere else; it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to ears, with thin roots and thick leaves. There are small ones and very large ones; I saw a man who had two on his stomach that looked more like fungi than anything else, without any difference between them, they were white, had thin roots, and had a split in them, and moisture flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them out and found one weighing 18 ounces and the other 6 ounces; the procedure for the incision is that you should examine whether the disease is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist with thin roots; then cut with a spatulum wide enough that the cautery can be applied with fire in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For many times there are dangerous bleeding issues when cutting, and if the blood flows, then quickly use cauterization; and if you see that the patient is frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made thread, tie the joint as we have said, and leave it for 2 days; then constrain it, and do not stop tightening the thread until it cuts the joint, and through it, there will be no pain; and if the roots are thick, then you may fearfully cut into the stomach, but you can cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the stomach which is a discolored color and has poor feeling and milk regurgitation.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these are encrusted abscesses, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers next.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of a boil comes from cauterization of a wound or from a fissure in the skin, and is on the abdomen and in some of the bowels, as happens in other routs, or from blood which flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from flatulence; and if it is through a rout in the skin and an exit from the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a minor thing without pain, and there are various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with their fingers, it springs back, and sometimes it is constricted, and grows larger at the entrance of the bath and from great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, and does not constrict; and if it is due to blood, then the abscesses are large and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to flatulence, there is puffiness upon touching, and the work is that you look to see whether the appearance is for blood from an artery or vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must let the wound heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is in the intestine or bowels, then you must instruct the patient to tighten his belt and be stretched out straight, then sign all around the swollen area; then instruct him to lie still between your hands, then go around the area that you have marked all around the spasm, then expose half of the abscess above the great nail; then tie it tightly all around with a strong thread or strong silk cord, and let the patient's hand hang loose; then open half of the abscess stretched over the string, and insert your finger, and feel for the intestine; if you find it caught in the string, then release it from the belt and bring the intestine out of the abdomen; and if you find the bowels, grab them at the nail and cut away the excess; and if the artery or vein is causing trouble, go around it neatly, then return to your task and take two needles, thread two strong wires through them, and insert the needles all around where you made the cross as though you were piercing it; then pull out the abscess in four places along the needles, and when you see it, remove the needles and leave the wound open until it drains, then cut away the dead flesh by itself; once it is thin and draining, clean the wound as needed, then draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound as appropriate, and sew up the wound.
dou chancre	the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the types of ulcers and how to treat them with medications, as well as the importance of cauterization with iron. Now, let's talk about ulcers that develop in the mouth, especially in the gums, and similar areas. It is important to treat these early on by removing any dead tissue. However, once they become larger and more established, it is best not to disturb them, as I have never seen one healed through such treatment, nor has anyone else as far as I know.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile sometimes; then make him bleed if he has manifest repletion, then prepare the patient .i. good place to perform the operation; then cut off the nails or calluses, and shave the hair all over, and remove the bone all over without leaving anything; and let the blood flow out completely, and squeeze the site well with your hand or something, and if the bleeding makes you hesitate about cutting the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed in the division the appearances of dropsy, and how the gathering of fluid occurs, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure which is performed by medication, and that which is cured by iron; only these two appearances are described: tympanites and hydrops, for these are mortal conditions. Therefore, when you treat this appearance of dropsy called "eclites" with medication, and the cure does not help, then consider whether the patient is weak, or if they have another illness other than dropsy, such as constipation and similar conditions; in that case, do not use iron, for there is doubt involved. But if you see a strong person suffering only from dropsy, and they are not too young or too old, then proceed as follows: raise the patient upright in your hands, and have an assistant press their abdomen to force the fluid to the lowest part of the feet, then take the spathumile spiny according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let there be a point, and yet not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when one inserts it, nor cause bleeding; then examine if the dropsy is in the intestines: if it is due to the disease of the liver, then your incision should be on the left side of the abdomen three fingers wide; and if it is due to the gallbladder, then the incision should be on the right side, and the patient must not lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not flow into that weak place; then pierce all the way through the skin with your instrument, and plug it up, and leave your hand on the whole spatumile between the skin and the syphon as in skinning to the thickness of a fingernail or nail; then pierce the syphon so that the spatumile comes out at the desired place, and this is the location of the water, then draw it out, and insert your instrument with which you made the incision into the spatumile, and remove the cause:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	It resembles a silver needle, and is made of brass or light bronze, and has a small hole in the lower part; and on one side there are three holes, on another two, and on the other one, and it is shaped like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes make when they cut feathers:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	at the top is the handle, so that when the instrument comes to the wound, it immediately descends upon the wound; therefore evacuate half or a third of its quantity, for if you evacuate more than is appropriate in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the shock of the instrument or he will faint or approach death; but evacuate according to the amount of his strength and according to what the dispositions of his strength indicate, and according to his pulse; then withdraw the instrument and retain the blood, and it is now retained by the membrane which blocks the hole that I mentioned, about which I have spoken, which you pierce according to this manner; then reintroduce the instrument the next day if you see the patient bearing it, and evacuate a little quantity of blood; do this every day, and beware of fainting until there remains but a little blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the disease, leave it a lot of water, and the cure is hot sand or earth, and by much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and by drinking; and the cure is with dessicative medicines until he is healed, and cauterize over the stomach and over the liver and over the spleen after the extraction of the fluid, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without an opening in their penis, or the opening is small and not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, then pierce it with a very thin spatulum according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place a small piece of lead in the opening and tie it and leave it for 3 or 4 days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug, and he will urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not necessary at all, because the urine that comes out does not allow the opening to close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose opening is small, if he is medicated with the cloth of lead, as we have said, it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in their place are blocked, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot reach the foreskin, and this is a serious disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of doing it is that the patient lies on his back, then the head and glans of the penis are made as large as a pena, with the opening in the middle as it should be; and take care to prevent bleeding which often occurs, and if it does, stop it with what stops blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these whitlows come on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must grasp them with a very small needle, and cut and clean them all, then put cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on them; then cure it with fine ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, discolored and putrid, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the ulcer is on the shaft of the penis, and part of it is inside and part outside, then you must first remove the ulcer that is inside; and when it is healed, treat the one outside.
