And if both hands emerge, then you must gently reset them little by little; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a chair, and lift her feet upward; then raise the chair off the ground, and lean her forward so she does not strain while standing; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child is dead, then press their hands with the nail as mentioned before, extract the child, and reset in the same way.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's issue upon his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on his feet, he should be pushed upward; then turn him slowly, until he is straightened out; then grasp one of his feet and stretch him out slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he leaps just up to the crotch, instruct him to grasp and cause the mother to sneeze; then if God wills it, he will leap out.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump out as we have said, then slowly turn it back and forth until it is in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not come out as we have described, take musk, altae oil, gum, and broil it all in the mortar; and apply this ointment to the mother's abdomen, then let her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is soft underneath, place the myrrh collar on her, and let her sit for an hour; then have her sit on a chair, then sneeze and squeeze her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for now the child will come out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	with the birth of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, he puts his hands on its head little by little; then he leans over its neck, and its feet hang down, and it lies on its back; and he bends his hands little by little, and then presses them on the belly, and removes the cushions underneath, until it is straightened out below; and if the child does not cry, he takes hold of its feet and moves them about, then he moves the belly upstream, then he blocks his hands in; and he rocks the child little by little; and he commands the woman to hold on until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child which comes from a width of one hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I will try to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed and raise her legs; then administer the mustard paste that I described earlier; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, then try to bring back the hand; then deliver the child as nature intended, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold on until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the emergence of the child onto its neck, and spread out his hands, and turn his face towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I desire the bailiff to dye his hand, then turn it little by little, and move it gently; and when it is even, he puts on the nature of mustard and oil, as we have said, then he commands that it moves little by little; and when you have done this, make him sit on a seat, and command that he grip; and make him sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all of the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way to all the afterbirth, then grasp the afterbirth with your fingernail, so that the moisture is emptied; and if the infant can reach his face and neck, grasp him from the side, so that he is not retained and dies; then insert the infant inside, so that you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to grip something a few times: then she will give birth easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the twin's birth
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; this is not a strange thing, but it happens seldom.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	These are strange things, and do not live, unless by name; I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the phlegm which divides them, which is bound to the brain; and sometimes they issue naturally like a tail, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue greatly, then the cure as we have said, and let the doctor be skillful, and do quickly and skillfully what she does; and do thus as it benefits the patient.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the brain, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the glorious sage, and it is necessary that the doctor know this, because sometimes similar things happen; so act according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman for a dead fetus or womb, as I have said in the previous section, and there is no movement, forcing you to use manual labor; then you must know whether the woman has good health and does not fear death. Then the woman should be laid on her back, with her head inclined downward and legs raised; and she should be given a enema with an injection tube in two parts, or she can lie down in bed so that she is not strained during the delivery of the child. Then rub the mouth of the mother with moist oils mixed with myrrh, fenugreek, and flax seed; then anoint her hands with these oils and myrrh; then gently insert the injection tube, and watch out for signs that the fetus is descending towards the head. Then insert the tube into its ears, neck, mouth, palate, under the beard, in the nostril, or near the sides; if the descent is towards the feet, insert it into the heel and the lower leg. The tube should be held with the right hand, and the bulb between the fingers of the left, and gently squeeze the bulb all the way to the fingers, then insert the tube into one of the places we have mentioned until it reaches the void; this is the shape of the tube:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then push against the other nail, or the third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then they are evenly pushed from one side to the other, to draw them out, and the nails are bit down to hold them in place, as this is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remains, then anoint the fingernail of one of his fingers with oil and rub it in that part, and pull out the other part; and if nothing remains, then put this nail or a higher one, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back due to the dislocation, then you must wrap it with a cloth until it is all out; then grab the joint of the palm or the wrist, and so you must do for the other hand, and for the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is stuck in the birth canal, where there is sharp pain gathered at the head, then you must use a spatulum between your fingers to loosen the head and draw out the fluid; or you may pierce it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one. And in the same way, do if the child has a large natural head; then pull on the bones with tweezers, and if the shoulder is stuck and strained, split it so that the fluids inside the narrow passage come out; and if it cannot pass, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the fluids run out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on his feet, the pull is slight, and the movement towards the mouth of the wound is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stuck in the belly or the birth canal, then you must strain it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and cut into the belly or the birth canal so that the fluids inside come out; and if other limbs are stuck, and the shoulder remains, then insert your finger into the mouth of the birth canal, and pull until the baby's head comes out; then grab its ankle or ankles, and pull them out. And if the mouth of the birth canal is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has formed there, one should not work on it, but instead apply moist and greasy remedies; and the provider applies poultices, and softens and moisturizes with water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is on its side, and you can bring it to an even position, then proceed as we have said for a live child; and if one cannot, then pull it out in pieces, leaving nothing of the afterbirth behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if pus comes out as we have said for abscesses that occur in the uterus; and if there is bleeding, then it should be treated with hot water, and other remedies should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I also saw a woman whose child had died in her womb, then she gave birth to another on top of it, and the other died as well.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she got an abscess in her armpit, which swelled up so much that it opened and began to discharge a lot.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the priest, and I thought for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong吸引plaster, and an bone came out, and after a few days, some more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled much, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I have used this treatment, and with it I have saved a woman's life; and she lived for a long time afterward, and only occasionally had a little pain in that place; and I have not known of this chapter failing when, upon discovering an unusual condition, the physician knew how to apply a remedy.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the dislocated joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the press, to which one applies books; and at two turns at each shoulder from the two lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the instrument should be more delicate if it is to be used with a restrictive forceps, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the forceps should be two digits wide, and the margin of the trees should be one-and-a-half digits long; and in both limbs there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are firmly attached to one another, each half a digit or a little longer; and these two adjustments are inserted into the uterus to open it when the two prongs are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with its appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of tweezers; and has at both ends two adjustments, as you see, a palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you see open the wound by all the instrument, then let the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging and her legs open, then fit together the two adjustments in the wound, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then work your hand on the whole instrument, as you have done with tweezers equally, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the wound, so that the midwife does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all decorated, and they have many similarities; and when the patient sees them prepared, he is more eager for the operation, and more confident due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair of the instrument until you have prepared it, for their need is不可避.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained in childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold back her breath, then make her sneeze with a scent, and pinch her nose and mouth with your hands; and if she vomits through this, that is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, they take the pot and make a hole in the lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as comfrey, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over fire; then they put one end of the tube into the pot and the other end into the mouth of the wound, and they apply it until the vapors enter the wound; then they make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then cut out the pus gently.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra. And if the mouth of the wound is closed, we have spoken of the cure for sneezing and of the fumigation of herbs; but if it does not heal from all that we have said, then beware of going astray in the treatment; but it is necessary to tie what is at the mouth of the wound to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse it with the ointment of the four-fold remedy, then she will discharge and recover, but nevertheless, when she discharges, a foul odor comes to the stomach and head, and the illness is cured.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So therefore appropriate fumigations are necessary: some of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.

de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without their navels pierced, but with the umbilical cord attached to a small, slender stalk; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this stalk with her finger, and not with a sharp instrument, and to guard against piercing the membrane; then she should put wet linen in wine and oil on it, then it will heal.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt it will heal, insert a wooden peg into the hole and leave it for several days, then remove it when the child wants to go in rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this filling comes suddenly from a wound or abscess; it should then be stopped suddenly: then it should be treated as we have said with the wooden peg.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula in the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodular and grow larger than those that come from within the anus, or in the space between the two parts, whether there is one fistula or several; and when this nodulation is old, it opens and emits moisture, a white discharge, or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent. They are perceptible by what comes out of them, either through evacuations or flatulence, when the patient passes gas, and sometimes they burst out suddenly.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pierce all the way to the bladder, and halfway down the penis; and they can reach the joint of the thigh, and up to the scrotum.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so one knows whether the fistula in the anus is persistent or not; and it is known by putting your finger into the anus, and pushing a thin needle made of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has a twisting, one puts in a thin rod made of lead or a horsehair until you feel the rod at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there comes no discharge, flatulence, or pus out of the opening as we have said, then know that it does not penetrate; so hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has pierced through to the bladder or the urinary tract, and the urine flows out, and cannot be stopped with medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived just to the joint of the thigh, then the vein is flowing just to the site; if there is no twist and the pain is located around it, then it has settled there and is not helped by medicine or ointment; and in these persisting fistulas, there is no cure other than labor and the folly of those who meddle.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not persisting and is not old, there is hope of recovery by iron, as I have experienced, and the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift his legs up to his thighs, and bend his thighs towards his belly; then insert a tent made of bronze or lead if there is twisting, until you know where the vein leads.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around his anus, then you must insert your index finger there if the vein has not yet pierced through; and examine where you feel a lump or a boil between your finger and the flesh, and thus you know that it is persisting; do not treat one who has such a condition.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can indeed heal some of them, but this happens rarely; and the aid that one provides is to heat the delicate cautery according to the size of the fistula, as has been said before; and put it all hot into the fistula, until it reaches the anus; and do this twice or three times, until you know that the false flesh, which resembles the feather of a bird, has been burned away; and then cure with moist tent fabric, until the flesh is gone, and then cure with ointment to close up and heal.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is healed thus, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is not healed thus, it cannot be otherwise; and if the tent enters and does not pierce all the way to the rectum, which is at the anus, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of flesh or pus, and you see the fistula following the covering towards the anus; then cut off the fistula at its beginning, and put in the cautery again before the tent, and then the cautery after, until it reaches the top of the tent; and the tent will be released and fall out; then remove those false fleashes that resemble a bird's feather, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus runs out, and cuts between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or with medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery draws together two things: that is, it burns the joined flesh and dries up the blood and moisture; then, treat the wound with moist tenting on butter or crushed substance until the skin oozes fluid and the burned flesh comes out in the fluid; then, treat the wound with ointments of hardened oil until the medicines dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way to the surface from the depths, and is distant from the body, put your finger or a plug in it, and probe it.

If you feel the tent, and between two is the thread or flesh, or it is close to piercing, there should be no fear or worry through administration of one of three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it down to the bone, or if you can, place tents and treat it as first described; do not go too deep so that you do not cut into the lining which holds the foundation, and let the evacuations occur through there willingly; then treat it as described; by chance it will heal. Or remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut away from the foundation, either with tents or another pointed instrument; then mend that injured flesh in the wound, and work to stop the fistula in the part distant from the foundation: this is a gentler method for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are created in this way: and it is when you drive the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side next to the foundation underneath the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and insert a twisted thread into it in two parts, and insert the tent all along the thread into the fistula as far as the tip.

If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that opening, so that you drive your finger into the foundation; and pull the end of the thread, and bring the two heads together, and tighten them against each other, and leave it for one or two days; and sometimes they are tightened until the threads cut through what is between them, and they separate; then cure the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, then make it open in every way you can, if it is not too deep.

Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spathula for creating a fistula is pointed at one end and smooth at the other; and on the one hand it is not pierced, so that one does not pierce what one should not, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some discharge blood, and there may be one or several of them, and they are outside the anus and at the top of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes there is a little yellow water or a little blood, and they are the color of the body; and the treatment for those who have them inside the anus is to instruct the patient to strain to go to the toilet until the veins break and the threads appear; then you can hurry and grasp it with tweezers, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots; and if the nails cannot hold it because of moisture, they are grasped with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camel's hair; and pull it out with your fingers, then cut it, and powder some hot powdered medicine on top that is suitable for cauterization; or you can cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauterization, then treat other hemorrhoids until he is healed; and if the anus cannot be cleared, then cleanse the patient with a strong and sharp enema to wash away what is inside the anus so that it can be cleared completely; when the patient strains, and if the threads come out of the anus, then the cure is easy; you grasp them with your fingernail or tweezers, cut them, then treat them as we have said until he is healed and fears incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must administer stitches in this way: take a twisted thread, and insert it into a needle, and then pull the thread through from the top, and pierce the needle on the other side; turn both ends of the thread beneath the needle, and keep it loose; then tighten the thread, tie a knot, and remove the needle. Do this for all the others, and leave one to stop any excess bleeding. Then place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate over the wound, and order the patient to rest; then let him lie there until he urinates, and when he has finished urinating, treat the wound with ointment and other remedies until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from dryness of the anus or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying up of the bowels within the intestines, due to the constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine fails.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must cut into the skin at the tip of a spur or your nail, so that it does not become moist; then treat it until it is dry as it should be; and if it cannot heal, then restart the bleeding more forcefully than before, until it heals completely and is scoured; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	where it trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ant is a small appearance formed under the body, and goes very deep; and sometimes the frost bites it, and they feel it like dead from trembling, and it comes throughout the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a feather of a goose quill, or a strong vulture feather, and place this feather on the trembling, so that the purple circle encompasses the trembling all around; then turn your hand over the entire feather, so as to rub all around the trembling, pushing it deeply in, and draw out the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that you should make it of a cane of brass or iron according to this form, and let it be thin underneath and drawn out on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that you can hold it with your fingers, and press it, And if you see, cauterize the tremor, as it is before in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or brass, or of molten copper or chainmail; and sometimes they are made small and large, depending on those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those which are administered for curing children, and who are feeble and suffering, are made small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is above broad; or the bellows are bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a division where the belly is tied, as you see, and the anus is pierced within; and it has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and the belly is made into a bag of beast skin or parchment, pierced all around with small holes, and between each opening there is an inch of space, then insert strong thread twisted in a cross or spiral pattern around the belly, like a thong; and when the medicine is inside, attach it to the instrument in front with a strong string, then catheterize; and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the syringe with oil or egg white, or similar, then insert it gently; then the minister should squeeze the syringe with both hands simultaneously until it is empty, then remove the syringe and let the patient lower his legs to the floor, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him squeeze as much as he can; and if he sleeps for a night afterward, it is even more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema him for a disease of descending stomach, and the medicine is in a hurry to come out, then let him strain until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the rectum or anus, then the syringe should be as fine as for a child; and this is how to make the fine syringe that the skin will not tear:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the cure of wounds; now we will discuss manual and medicinal cures according to their accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and what makes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are the piercing of stones, and the cutting of swords and knives, or lances, staves, arrows, and similar objects; and they can occur anywhere on the body, such as a wound on the neck, head, leg, belly, liver, and similar organs; and I will tell you how to cure each type of wound, starting with wounds on the head, since their treatment will be described in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from a blow of stone or similar things, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large, and you easily doubt a hot abscess: then make him bleed from the cephalic vein immediately if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction of the injured part; and prevent the patient from drinking wine and eating heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, then let his food be diminished, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put sorb on the wound, if hot abscesses come, cotton moistened only in rose oil or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put powder on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air; and if the burn has moved him, then put some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword, and the lips cannot be brought together by sutures, then bring them together by stitches, as I will say for wounds in the abdomen, from the ribs.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it can be probed, and it only hangs on by a little bit, then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find pus in the skin, and it is not near the bone, then probe and drain all the pus, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which does not clot, and it cannot be stopped with medicine, then ligate the artery, and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: you should apply this powder that heals as soon as the scorch has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take incense one part, dragon's blood two parts, quicklime three parts, and powdered very finely, and apply it to the wound, and press it firmly so that it becomes well-adhered and united with all its blood; then bind it tightly, and leave it without removing, if it does not become swollen; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with chalk alone, when one doesn't have incense or dragon's blood, but the wound has been burned.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, especially in this way, do not put any of this powder on it; but place some digesting ointments, or a poultice made of barley flour, water, and honey, until it is healed; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if there is a bone fracture with the wound, and it is small, I will extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you about fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, there is nothing else to do but let the cure happen, and not put anything constricting on it, because it hurts the nerves and makes them withdraw; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but the medicine should be beneath, like a cold wash in lukewarm water, and mixed with rose oil, and cooked wash also in lukewarm water, and other stones of the same kind, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut it and tie it with bands, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is chapped and full of pus, then pierce it or a lower place; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, then bind it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the larynx, and the windpipe is blocked, preventing the meat from going down, then cut the larynx on the cane of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then bind it properly, and leave it for a few days, then treat with ointments until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then pierce it; and if there are pieces of bone, then draw them all out if you can, and those that you cannot reach, then leave them until the wound becomes purulent and is relieved, and ligate the wound; and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder I have described.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine whether the wound bleeds at all: thus you know that the wound is deadly; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it for the blood which trickles out profusely, and returns to the body, and chokes off the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then put old cotton into the wound to suck up moisture, and let the patient sleep with his head on the wound for three or four, or more days; thus there will come no spasms, nor bad tremors of the body, nor convulsions. And when you see good signs, you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure it therefore with tenting and other remedies, until it is healed; and if it cannot be healed, and the wound is still open, then you know there is a fistula; so cure it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, in front or behind, then cure it as with that which is before; if it is large, then stitch it; and if it is small, then powder it, and if it is depressed into the bone, and pieces have been knocked out, then clean the wound, and draw out the foreign bodies if they are loose; and if they are not loose, then let the wound fester so that extraction will be easier; and for other wounds in other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from a rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	There are many types of hernia: some occur in the great wound, some in the small, and some in both. The great wound sometimes causes the intestines or nerves of the intestines to protrude through it; stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because it is harder to stitch up the intestines little by little when they are inflamed by the cold; they swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they are harder to stitch, and a small wound is better in this case because you can stretch the intestines back into place more easily. There are four types of abdominal hernia: two common types occur with stitching up the abdomen, and the other two types are specific to other wounds on the body; nonetheless, they are also applicable to abdominal wounds, and I will explain each type.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine has come out, and there is a desire to put it back, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in such a way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in warm water only, or cook it in water with squills and cypress and spike lavender, and swab the intestine until the swelling is relieved; sometimes this wine constrictor is made, and it is poured out solely to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling leaving, moisten the intestine with water or old wine in which mallows and marigolds have been cooked; for through this there is an adhesion to the entrance of a little thing. And if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is preferred over cutting, which one must not do without great necessity; and the instrument for splitting is: cut inside at the curve and push out, and see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, he puts them back in according to their natural form in their proper place, if you have the strength to do so, because this is much better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is low in the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs above his head; and if it's high in the abdomen, he should lie down with his head and feet lower than the rest of his body, and if the rupture is on one side or the other, then he should be positioned so that the wounded part is higher. And you must apply what I say to large and small wounds alike.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you have at hand and hold in your hand a pair of forceps that touch all around the wound, and this is how you should sew: thread an needle or several according to the size of the wound, leaving two fingers' width from the top of the wound, then insert an needle through both sides of the skin below the skin, going through the skin itself, and pierce it in that spot, then tie off the thread around the needle with a double thread; then bring the two sides of the wound together gently, and then leave another two fingers' width, and insert another needle; then tie the thread around this second needle as you did the first, and keep doing this according to how many needles you need, until the entire wound is closed. The needles should be medium-sized, not too thin or too thick, so that they can pierce through the skin and flesh without reopening the wound; then bend the needles so they don't scratch the patient when he sleeps, and attach tents or pieces of cloth to the ends of the needles to hold them in place, leaving them until the wound is healed. This method of sewing with needles is best for small wounds, as a single needle or two will suffice. The second method of sewing is common, and it involves holding the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the subcutaneous tissue together with one needle and a strong thread; once you have pierced all four layers, bring the needle back to where you started, as if you were sewing a garment; leave a distance of a minor finger between each stitch. This sewing method works for both men and women, and I used it on a man who had been stabbed in the abdomen; the wound was more than a palm wide, and his intestines protruded two palms out, and the wound was in the middle of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back his intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up until the 15th day, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they had judged him to be dead, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where there was no medicine or ointment; and I put clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water and honey until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you about the two proper ways to sew: take the needle and push it from the outside through to the inside; when it has pierced right through, hold the thread where it emerges on the inside and pull it through from the other side until the outside is touched again; the idea of this sewing is that you sew just as the leather-workers sew pelts, leaving a little thread on one side and then taking it up on the other, until the seam is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, which Galen describes properly, is like that used by some to join two pieces of cloth together naturally, and they apply one end of the thread to the other, in such a way: insert a needle at the tip of the wound nearby, and pierce only that spot, leaving the two ends of the wound; then turn the needle and pierce from the outside part inward to the inside, through both ends of the wound; then pierce one and then the other from the outside part inward to the inside, in two other tips of the thread that are on the other side; and this is the mother method of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and some testify to it: one should sew the belly with two needles, with thread in each; and one should insert one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and know that when the hernia is in the abdomen, the sewing is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgement of the wound is the same as the judgement of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, so that the burn has moved, then put back the intestine, and the membrane; then put on the powder, and if the burn has moved, put on some ointment, as long as the wound bleeds; then tie the thread, and sew up the edges, and the lip; then cure the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicine, put on, as soon as it begins to bleed, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you don't need any other medicine in various dispositions when wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will affect the principal members, then it is necessary to moisten light linen in tempered warm oil, or rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if there is pain or swelling in the bowels, and it happens many times, then cleanse them with a clyster of tepid black wine, and likewise if the swelling comes up to the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines, which are called 'young', cannot heal when they are raw, and this is due to the thinness of the veins through which they are, and the subtlety of the whole body, and their proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the skin jumps out of the wound, then put it back as you would with the intestines, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you should tie off the area which is black so that no blood flow comes from it, for there are veins and arteries in it; then cut what is between the stitch, and place the two sides hanging down from the part under the wound until extraction when the skin slips, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the road of boiling
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are ruptured, and the wound is small, then one can heal it in some people, for I saw a man who was pierced in the belly with a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and was swollen and became a fistula, and from it came digestion and flatulence; I applied a poultice according to what I could, and did not cease subtilizing until it healed and the edges joined.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him bleeding, I doubted that the patient had pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a way: take a large testicle, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the testicle has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it squeezes its mouth shut; and then tie the testicle, and it will stay as it is so that it cannot come undone, then put another testicle after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and heal the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If it bleeds in the intestines and does not harm the patient, one can tie the intestines with a thin thread cut from an animal's intestine, in this way: take the tip of the intestinal thread that is very dry, then tie to the tip of the thread a fine linen thread twisted tightly, then insert the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and pull it shut; and this method of sewing with testicles is not effective except according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the grail-like intestines, there is nothing that helps except skill.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and becomes bow-shaped.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the green node, a hard and white swelling, where there is no pain, and is like the comb of a bird; sometimes it is clearly swollen, and sometimes thick; sometimes small, and sometimes large; and I have already spoken about these causes, and their signs, and the cures for medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you about the treatment of a fistula that is done by hand.
