Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and from arteries, and from nerves, or from the sinus, or from the intestines, or from the bladder, or from any of the sides, or from the spine of the back, or from any joint of the hands or feet; and if it comes to the principal property of the primary member, and in similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of grief and healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it being understood, then take an iron or bronze tent, if the fistula is straight, so pick it up; and if the fistula is crooked, then search with a thin tent of lead, for the lead bends around the crookedness; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot well search it with tents, then cleanse it by enema through one of the openings, for moisture cuts from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then pick it up bleeding as hard as you can, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and see how deep it is, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and where he feels it; and when you know for certain the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or any of the places I told you, then treat it according to what I have told you, and remove the rotted matter and corruption that is inside; and then heal it as it heals, and if the fistula is very deep and straight, then you must pick it up as much as you can, then place moist tents soaked in medicine water, and put them into the fistula to the head, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments to clean flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then pick it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve causes you no pain in the limbs, as we have said, and if the bone is exposed and there is decay and darkness, then treat it as follows: cut out the decayed part, then treat the wound with healing remedies until it is healed; and if it is not healed, return to the previous treatment, understanding that you have not yet reached the bottom. Then explore and dig until you reach the bottom, remove all the decay, then restore the area; and if it is healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, understand that the decay is too deep for you to reach; then do nothing but let nature take its course; and if there is a small decayed bone, and you can pull it out with tweezers, then extract it with the appropriate instrument for this purpose, and if there are several bones, pull them all out, not leaving any behind. And if moisture causes you problems, and there is no doubt or fear, then cut out the moisture and decay, and heal the wound.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place something over the wound to promote swelling, and let it swell around the bones, and then the bones will come together more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, then clear away the corruption only until the blackness is gone, then dress the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption, and it reaches down to the bone marrow; then it must be cut and covered all the way to the corruption, and then the wound treated until it heals. And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid from this in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from inside the body, so that the materials came to the leg and swelled into a large abscess, and there was no way to drain it; but the doctors, through their foolishness, worked on it until the abscess burst, and much material flowed out, and it became a fistula, and there were many openings from which flesh and moisture from the body flowed; and many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine, so that I was called to him, and saw his leg and the remedies with which he was treated, and what flowed out through the openings into a great illness; and the skin of the young man turned red, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of the holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one came against another throughout the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened therefore, and probed one of the holes until I exposed a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption extended to the bone within; I applied what appeared to me to be necessary for the corrupted bone, and believed that there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and then I began to heal the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but could not close it; so I began again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and applied treatment to it, and then removed it, and labored to close the wound; but I could not, though I probed around the bone for a palm's width, and drew it out entirely from its socket, and then restored it with medicines; and it healed quickly, and needed no further probing except because of the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurred, but he was completely healed, and a hard lump grew in place of the bone, and he had a good disposition and no harm or contrary pain anywhere, neither when lying down nor when rising up.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, it should be bound in this way: take a thread and bind it to the head of the open bone, and command someone to pull it upward; and tie another longer piece of linen over the thread, and place it over the lump that has grown on top of the bone, and draw the thread so that you draw the corrupt lump underneath downward, and uncover the flesh above where you see it is being bound, so that the thread does not cut into the flesh; and place a hot iron or a flat object underneath the bone to cover the corrupt lump; and one must bind it as tightly as possible as far as one can see and feel the corruption, and then bind it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is broken and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh; then put a hot iron underneath, and then press the corruption from one side to the other, and press it with the palm of your hand from the edge of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupt joint, and press on the bone where it contains it on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of both joints, there is no need to cover it; and if the corruption is in the knuckle of the hand or foot, that thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must inquire into this corrosion, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in every way you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not harm you; and know that there are many knives and probes for covering these bones, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of them, their thickness and thinness, and size and smallness, and hardness. And therefore one must prepare for each appearance of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the instrument which you need, according to what it needs.
dou feu	by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head can be dislocated due to internal causes or external forces; and when you have treated this corrosion with medicine, but it does not help, then cover the affected member up to the point where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil, from the defect in the member; and the signs are that the member becomes black, as if burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corrosion spreads from one member to another, and affects the whole body; so be quick to cover it, and if it is due to the bite of venomous creatures, such as the scorpion fish and adder, and similar, if the corrosion is on the head, then cover it, and do not give it any space to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, then cover it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not spread to the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is fatal, and there is no remedy except in proportion to the amount of its virtue; and thus one should act when the corrosion reaches the foot: if it reaches the first joint, then cover it after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, then cover all of the foot; and if it climbs up the leg, then cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy except to cut off the limb and let the patient die; and the method of covering the limb with a bandage is that you tie it above and below, and stretch one rod from the upper tie, and another rod from the lower tie, and you loosen the flesh that is between the two ties by as much as a span, so that the bone is exposed; then cover it with a bandage, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the bandage does not touch the healthy part, and bring the patient another wound and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if there is bleeding when you operate, cauterize the site gently, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete. Then bind the wounded member with a suitable bandage and cure it until it heals. And I will tell you what happened to a man in his sleep: he had a blackness that looked like a burn, and this corrosion started at the big toe of his foot, so that it affected the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered his foot and was healed. A long time after, the corrosion returned to his finger on his hand, and he came to me, and I applied some reflective remedies after purifying the body, but he could not stop the corrosion. And he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to because I had no hope of removing the matter. And I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for his vital forces were weak. And he despaired entirely and returned home, covered his hand, and was healed. I have told this story only so that others may learn from it if they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	At times an abscess forms in a fleshy spot, and remains so long that it causes a great gathering of pus; then it erupts and pierces, and the pus escapes, leaving a hollow like a vessel; the skin above is as thin as a piece of cloth, and does not heal up to the bone or nerve; such a condition is called "sain" and not "fistula". But if it becomes so prolonged that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called a "fistula"; and one covers this skin all around, and especially when it is thin, like a piece of cloth; and it does not heal over due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have confidence that the skin is healing and the corruption is not in depth, and the flesh is thick, then cure it with a clyster thus: look to see if the breast is swollen, and the pus within has an foul odor; then clyster it with Egyptian medicine made thus: take equal parts of alum, oil, and litarge, and put them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and as thick as honey; then take some according to your need, and dilute it in water and honey, and clyster the breast, and close the opening; leave the medicine for two hours, then express it out; do this many times until the breast is cleaned out and the foulness removed. And if Egyptian medicine is not available, then you may clyster with ashes of vine wood: take ashes from vine wood and pour water over them, then strain it and use it to clyster until you know that the breast is cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear the Egyptian medicine, or ash water, then clyster with water and honey in which there is a little litarge ground in; or you may clyster with honey and wine mixed, for the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and wine makes the sain dry up; and when you have done this and are confident that the breast is cleansed, then clyster it with something which causes flesh to form within it; take diaphoretic plaster and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you may clyster with other medicines and ointments of which I have spoken in the section on ointments. And if the opening of the breast is small, so that the clyster rod cannot enter, then enlarge it a little with an iron, and insert a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon; and if the wound is too large, then cut away only enough so that the clyster can enter; and if the pus-duct which drains the pus is above, then close it higher up, or lower down.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowels are in perfect health, one should not leave charred matter inside; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, arrange things so that the bowels move to the lowest place they can, for when the bowels are healthy, one should not leave charred matter inside, and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, arrange things so that the bowels move slightly downward, and do not leave anything of the bowels; take strengthening medicines to put over the wound, and have linen bandages covering all of the wound; then press strongly at the opening of the breast, making it a little larger than before, and apply a soothing ointment on the other bandage according to the size of the opening, and place it over the opening of the wound to ease the bowels, and do not remove the large bandage for several days; and that which is over the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the bowels, and know what comes from the bowels, whether venom, pus, or digested or undigested food; take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises over the wound, then know that the breast is healing, and draw closer to health; and then loosen it in the morning, or the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change the other bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows abundant and unchanged after many days, know that the breast is not drying up.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons spread over a long time, do not despair of your health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	Because there are people who have gradual healing of flesh in their wounds, and some who heal quickly; and if a wound on the breast does not heal after many days, know that the breast will not heal; and if the wound is slow to heal and is distant, then prepare dry medicines moist in substance but dry in virtue, like an ointment with diaphoretic properties, because it contains a large amount of vitriol, and this is the best medicine. Take an ointment with diaphoretic properties, and make it with rose oil, and rose wine equal in substance; then cook it and use it. And the same is done with thickened honey, when diaphoretic ointments are not available, or take myrrh, aloe, and incense, powder them, and mix with the honey as I said before, and use it. If the wound is slow to heal, and is not healed by this treatment, then you know that the corruption is deep, and it creates an impression in the bone, or in the hard tissues, or in the soft tissues; so the treatment for a fistula wound, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaritis is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the hand or foot, or sometimes in other places; and when it becomes infected, and no attention is paid to it, then it becomes a large abscess, and it runs and oozes pus as far as the root of the nail, and sometimes all the way to the bone; and corrosion occurs up to the bone, causing a putrid pain, and the area around the nail becomes swollen, and the color turns yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then you should cut away all the dead tissue remaining under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy; and if the nail grows into the flesh, and it starts to hurt and blister, then you should put a needle under the nail pushing the flesh up, and cut away the dead flesh gently and carefully, and apply burning and corrosive medications to remove everything; then treat the wound with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and draw it out, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see it corrupting, cut it open at one of its ends as it has been said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it becomes ulcerated and pus-filled, and he feels great pain, then you must heal him first; then cut the nail of the finger of the spatumile diagonally from above, and be careful that the cutting does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something soothing on it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a deaf hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two types of warts that grow on the hands of some people by chance are all fleshy, and by chance they have bones, and sometimes they have nails, and some grow at the root of the joint, or their origin is in one of the fingers of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any nerve of the head does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the neck, by chance moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is slight, in such a way: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; so you must keep it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For he who is born in the nerve of the head, you must first shave the flesh around it roundly to the bone, then shave the bone with a suitable thread for that, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Joints that come together come by birth, or by wound sewing, or by burns, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you must cut the suture so that the nerves are restored according to their natural forms; then place between two tents or dripping wet cloths in rose oil so that they do not stick together; or place between two pieces of fine plank, until the sutures are healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If sealing occurs on either palm with the fingers, cut that stitch as needed.
des vils	of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large wrapped vessels full of melancholy superfluities, which come to many parts of the body; and they occur more in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer an emetic to him once or twice, and then heal him with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with fire is in two ways: one is that they are cauterized, and the black blood is drawn out; and the other way is to lift the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this way: first heat the leg with very hot water until the large veins are dilated, then draw the leg from the thigh to the knee, then make an incision in one place, or two or three places, with a broad cut, then open and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can tolerate; then ligate it and command that he eats foods causing constipation with black bile; and start the evacuation and bleeding again when the veins are full, and bind the wound.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The preparations for the patient are as follows: raise the leg of the sick person, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in the bath, and heat the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you don't have a bath, then heat it over the fire, and then press down on the vein from the top to the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin at the nail, and scorch the vein on each side, so that it appears when you feel it; and you will see it red and black, and when it goes into the skin it looks like a white cord; then tie off the vein from below, so that it is raised out of the skin, and then let it go gently at the nail, then press it in another place above three times; then scorch the skin over the vein until it appears, then let it go towards the nail, as you did before; then make another incision, or several if you need to, then lift it, and press it down at the toe, then pull and lift it up to the second incision; then draw it out from incision to incision, until it is completely out, then bandage it; and if you cannot pull and raise it, then tie a strong double thread around it, and tie and pull it, and tie it under the vein, and turn your hand from side to side so that it comes out; and be careful not to burst it, because if it bursts, it cannot be pulled or raised, and it will harm the patient; and when you have treated it completely, then put soft wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound site, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the eye is constricted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one covers the eye is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cover the vein; and it is a large curve, because if it were subtle, it would cover the vein, but it must be large as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is stranded in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens with the pustules that come under the skin, just as serpents and worms come inside the body, stranded between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then the color changes, and the wound begins to come out, as well as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the wound opens, you should wrap around it a piece of plaster three and a half to two inches wide, and tie it, leaving the plaster hanging down on the leg, and every time some comes out from under, wrap the plaster around the leg again, and if it is too long, cut off part and wrap around what remains, but do not cover the root as long as it is all coming out; for if you cover it, it will enter into the flesh and cause an abscess and swelling in the area, because of which thing it should be treated little by little until the head, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this wound is as long as five or ten palms, and a man came to me once whose was twenty palms long, and when you cover it, it makes a hole or cavity, and penetrates all the way through, so that everything comes out, and the matter within is evacuated, and soothing medicines are applied to the spot for several days, and then it is cured as abscesses are.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein opens in the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself, and much pus comes out, and it drains freely; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms which grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "cow disease" in our land because it often occurs in cows, and it is caused by a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, moving throughout the body, ascending and descending, until it erupts through the skin, and it usually comes out through the eye; and it is caused by putrid humors, as with roundworms, tapeworms, and other parasites in the belly. It is feared for its malice, for when it moves through the body and reaches the head, it can enter and destroy the eye, and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and pulled, one cannot help but wait until it bleeds: therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong string, tie it tightly, then press on it and pull it out forcefully; and if the pus is deep in the flesh, and you do not draw it out, cauterize it with fire until it comes out; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye, tightly constrict under the eyelid, then press on it and pull it out forcefully; and one must use cleansing remedies for the body from soluent medicines to draw out the putrid humors, and use poultices of warming meats.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "farting" in our language, and it is a pain that occurs in some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm; and a little later, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, as bright as silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later ran through the whole body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that she was spinning around the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much at how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease progress in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have seen many whose pain moved from one place to another, but I did not see it in the woman; and I thought that it was because women have dry bodies, and their veins are exposed, and this wind is constrained to appear; and it does not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then tie it above and below tightly, and then press on it until that windiness constrained in its place issues; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it yourself, then have it treated by one who releases windiness, as with foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse according to their appearance and according to the part of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity is that there are some with large points, and small, and hooked, and fused; and some with two angles, and some with tongues, and some with parts; and they split in a member in two ways: either in a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls in any part of these limbs, and the sign of death that I will tell you about later appears: then you must be wary of extracting this arrow, because death comes afterward in many cases; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not completely embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces the bone and penetrates the brain, and there is a bleeding from the nose which is on top of the brain, and scotomata, and deafness, and blindness, and inflation, and redness of the tongue, and spasms, and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of blood; and perhaps also fluid comes out of the nose or ears; and sometimes they lose their speech and voice; and from the wound there is white moisture like pus, and also bruise-like blood; and if this sign appears to you, then cease the treatment and pull out the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the seventh when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were pierced by a hard object, not hollow; and sometimes the seventh becomes mute like the pulses, and expels black blood, and brings on chilliness and cold sweat, and syncope: then know without doubt that death ensues.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never leaves the lung is that there are no blisters around the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes colour, and gasps for breath and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits in the covering of the foot, then it is between the small ribs; and there is great swelling and pain, and gasping; and all the limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, by chance some indigestible food may jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the belly and nothing comes out through the intestines but feces, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow hits the bladder and urine spurts out and the patient dies, the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, spine of the back, hip, thigh, and leg, and similar members, are safe according to several arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in a nerve or artery and is not poisonous, as I will tell you about what happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	A certain man had an arrow shot into his jaw at its root near the ear; I probed it and pulled it out from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any bleeding.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow from under the skin of the eye, below the eyelid, in a man who had been shot; and the arrow was stuck, and only its tip was visible, pointing towards the nose; the arrow was as thick as an archer’s thumb, and all its feathering was gone; the man was healed and suffered no ill effects.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears; I removed the barbs and pulled gently until I extracted it, and the Christian recovered.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I extracted an arrow from a man's home that had pierced his stomach, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days passed, his condition did not improve; so I cut into the arrow, dislodged it, pulled it out, and he experienced no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a person with an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound is sewn shut on top; and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions remain unchanged, and he experiences no discomfort in any of his natural acts.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you will see another person with an arrow pierced through his face, and the wound is sewn shut; and he remains like that without suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow wound in the home of the prince, the king, who had an arrow lodged in his eye, and it was slightly inclined towards the right side; and the arrow was completely lodged for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it with a fine probe and felt nothing, but he felt a burning sensation under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed a soothing and digestive poultice on the site to reduce inflammation, and the location of the arrow became apparent to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for several days, and the wound healed quickly, but the patient experienced the presence of the arrow in his eye for a long time; he himself told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open and I probed it, feeling the head of the arrow which protruded; then, with the medicine, I widened the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow appeared clearly; within four months, the wound healed well. Then, I reopened the wound, pushing in tweezers, and probing with my fingers on both sides, but it would not come out; so, I did not cease to probe and use various instruments until one day, I was able to grasp it with well-made tweezers, as will be described at the end of this chapter, and extracted it, healing the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And those who saw the patient believed that the cartilage of his nose could not be restored; so, I restored it, and the wound was sutured, and the patient fully recovered.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Here I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you place your treatment on what I do not say, because books cannot understand everything; but wise masters compare well with little great things, and with what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows strike the members where they are pierced in two ways: either through the place where they enter or through another part; and that which jumps out from where it enters is an arrow entering into fleshy places, and sometimes jumps out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump out right away, then leave it as long as the flesh around it becomes rotten and the exit is relieved; and similarly, if it is pierced into the bone and cannot come out, then leave it for several days, and move it every day; and then it will jump out, and if it does not, then pierce it all the way through with a very thin tool, until the opening around it becomes enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned are apparent in the patient: then do not extract it, but leave it until it is even with the skin after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the brain, this is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck in the bone at all, but only in the flesh, and does not reach the brain, and the patient remains for several days without any bad symptoms, then treat it by extracting the arrow.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is lodged deeply and cannot be removed, then administer cauterization around the wound, as I have told you; then treat the site until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged deep in the body so that you cannot see it, then probe the entire wound; and if you feel it, extract it with an appropriate instrument; but if due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then cut open the wound widely; and if there is a barb on the arrow preventing its removal, cut off the shaft as close to the skin as possible, then bend or twist the barb so that you can extract the arrow; be careful not to break the arrow, which would make extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot in one go, then leave it until the area around it is swollen, and then pull it out, because the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood makes it contrary, then bring about what we have said about its treatment in its chapter; and beware of incising the nerve and of opening the vein, and put the wound how you can best pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that he was in when the arrow fell into him, for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes out from another part, or something appears from it, or the skin is swollen in that place if one sees or feels it apparently: cut there, so that the tweezers can grab it, and then pull it out: let it flow out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand rapidly, as far as it goes into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it again, and then try pulling it out again until it comes out; and if the arrow is in its shaft, then insert it all the way in; and if the shaft is broken, and you see that there is room for an instrument, then insert the instrument with a hooked point, so that the tip of the arrow goes into the hook of the instrument; and then pull it out, and if the arrow is hooked, then insert the instrument with its point entering in, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, you must cut all around the flesh where the poison is, as much as you can, then cure the wound as best you can.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces the buttock or thigh or belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut over it, cut out the poison; but be careful not to cut into the vein or nerve, then pull it out, and then stitch the wound, if necessary; and cure it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to treat arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and you should see the shape here:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the head of an arrow is like that of a bird's feather, to push on the point of the arrow, just as this shape shows:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pushing and probing if it is there:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one can bleed, of which there are XVI in the head, namely: II batans located behind the ears, called the two 'ear-veins'; and II temples that are visible on either side; and II veins in the corners of the eyes, called 'aspires'; and the vein located in the middle of the forehead; and the vein at the tip of the nose; and the two small veins in the neck; and II veins above the lips, called 'augeherich'; and II veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the neck, and the common people call it the 'vein of the head'; and the middle one is called the 'fast' vein, and it consists of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the common people call it the 'vein of the heart'; and the basilic vein is on the right side of the neck, and the common people call it the 'vein of the belly', and it is above the fossa, and it is that one from which one bleeds, which opens clearly above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvator vein is that which is between the auricular and annular veins, and they both have two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the curve of the armpit on the left side of the neck, and the second one is at the ankle on the right side of the neck; and the vein which is called the 'nether', which is at the ankle on the other side.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of veins that are behind the ears is helped by old cathartic remedies and by blistering; and the qualities of the bloodletting instrument, as I have told you, and it is that you should press the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then constrict the patient's neck with a bandage, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending from the head; then hold them tightly with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, prick deeply; then lift your hand all along the vein upstream, and pierce both skin and vein thoroughly with the lance, and let blood flow until you see it; then constrict and ligature it, so that it is healed; and I have already described incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries in the two temples is good for treating old migrainous headaches, and for sore eyes and habitual conjunctivitis, and for agony in the body of the eyes; and the quality of the bleeding is as I have said: and it is that the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins are clearly visible; and feel the pulse underneath your finger, and then sign with your finger; then lift the skin above the vein on your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up, and stop the bleeding as you have done in the other veins; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their binding and their release at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding from the vein in the forehead is as good as the bleeding from the cephalic vein for ancient diseases of the face, and for migraines and redness; and the qualities are such that the patient turns his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called 'fosseur', of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point over the vein and press gently with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the amount you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and sometimes the operation is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too sharp; and the patient must not move about, for the bone is near, and by chance the flames might break when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the jaw helps teeth, and for tinea, and redness, and eye pain, and diseases of the face; and the qualities of their bleeding are such that the patient turns his neck by twisting some ligament, as before; then bleed him, and let the bleeding be through the cross-vein, a little from the long vein with a slightly wide flame, because there is no flesh.
