Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, they may break; then let blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind it with a thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein on the nose is good for headache, and for sudden madness, and for facial diseases, such as migration and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then squeezes his nose with his left hand, and takes a long, thin flame, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it up for a night, for it is soon restored; and this is the way of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two sinuses helps with the constriction of the throat, and with the beginning of hoarseness, and many diseases, and with impetigo, and with corrosion, and with herpes, and with ulcers; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck underneath both sides, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient seated on a chair, then bleed the vein of the long one fairly widely, then draw the blood gently, or as much as is needed; then do the same in the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and squeeze both veins gently so that the patient does not choke; and let it be until morning, so that the wound can heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding from the gums
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding from the veins of the lips helps with sores in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and splitting of the lips, and pain in the teeth and gums.Si li sainie des leivres soit par tuit li corps, si convient qu’on l’estreigne a la fin; car il adont a meins et a membrains.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of bleeding are to have the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized by their being black, and by there being small black veins around them: press both of these, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, press the thickest vein on each side, and similarly do the same with the two above and below, for it is a similar process.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of bleeding under the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Bleeding from the veins under the tongue helps after bleeding from the head, and it aids in constrictions of the throat, and in diseases of the throat, and of the mouth; and the qualities of the bleeder are that the patient should sit between your hands facing the sun, and stick out his tongue, and look underneath on each side for a black vein: press both of these, and do not go too deep, because arteries are underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck from which one usually bleeds are healed in two ways: either by pricking with a wide flame-hot needle, or with an olivary needle as thin as a vein trenchant, and is called 'anesil'; and they are wide and thin according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is very famous, and it is broad as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the flat veins of the head that contain gross and troubled blood, with a wide flame-hot needle. And this is the shape of the olivary needle:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and subtle, and it is used for bleeding the subtle veins where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, aids in maladies that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and the bleeder must bleed freely, and be careful not to pierce the artery beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he pierces the artery, and there is a gushing of blood, then he must stop it, as I have said; and the needle must not be flame-hot, but tailed like an anesil.Et li auter sainie dou col est la zavaque, qui va desuz li menton si com le fraiz dou sainor qu’il saine li voinne dou col; et covient qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desuz.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basil does not open obviously, then you must stretch it, and change to another; or you want some from him, or heal in his place the vein in the arm: it opens obviously; and the flame copes silence, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place of bleeding, then you must stretch the arm so that you feel the pulse; then sign the place inside, and then tie the arm, and stop the vein with the flame silent; and beware that you do not harm the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rising up as high as urine in a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: hurry then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens; tie the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move it until it is healed. And let him be in fear, and do not move it until he is cured.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not staunched and he bleeds out and there are no medicines available, cut into the artery to stop the flow of blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of bark from the root of a fig tree, and split it, and take one half and bind it tightly until the next day; if the bleeding has stopped then that is good; if not, then treat it with a styptic powder as we have said, to stop the flow of blood. Stypic powders are not harmful for most conditions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The wound in the middle if it helps to draw out blood from the head and body above it, because it is composed of basil and cephalic, as we have said; and the surgeon must be careful of the nerve underneath, not to cut too deeply, and to find the nerve, which may become inflamed and damaged beyond repair; and this nerve often opens up in some men due to its subtlety, and if it does not open at all in others, then you must treat it with an instrument made for this purpose; and explore the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, they will make an incision there.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The sinus of the cephalic [vein] if it aids, draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes; and one should bleed with a flame of olive or myrrh, for it is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one should seek the lightest place, and not worry if one fails the first time, and one should try again; and by chance, the places inflame some men, when one fails the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding depends on your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done only to cure diseases but also to prevent them; and bleeding should be done in one of the three veins: the cephalic, the fast, and the basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of lent, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of digestion are apparent; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The medicine that is administered to the sick has no fixed time, but when there is a need during the day or night, at all times and in all seasons; and children should not be bled until they are fourteen years old, nor should women who are pregnant more than seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly over 60 years old be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever manner, they should cleanse the intestines with a mild enema if they have much retained stool, so that the veins do not attract harmful excess fluids from the intestines to the principal limbs; one should not bleed those who are very full from food, or those who are drunk, until they have sobered up, nor the very elderly; and if someone is bled after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, or excessive sexual activity with a woman, and from hard work, watching all night, fasting, or exertion of any kind, and whatever weakens the body through illness or injury; then subtly draw off the humors, if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicine, if you have the skill; then enter the bath, if nothing else can open up the veins to let out the blood, in order to cleanse it, and bleed from the vein on the ankle just below the ankle bone, as we have said; and guard against exertion that day, and sexual intercourse, and similar activities; and be calm and cheerful, and have the bleeder stand higher than the person being bled, and rub their arm two or three times to make the veins swell and become visible; then moisten the blade of the bleeding instrument with a little old oil, and place the tip of their left thumb over the vein where they want to bleed, so that the vein does not slip away from the blade.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flow like cords to the heart, and some that are filled with winds, so that when one applies fire, it retreats from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if the vein opens, the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be cautious in such cases.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is working for the first time, it is good; if not, try again a little lower down or higher up, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the part is swollen and the patient is in doubt, leave it for one or two days without binding the arm; perhaps hot abscesses will form; do not enter the bath then, but start the bleeding again if she wishes; and if the opening is small, cut the vein short and gently, and you doubt that it will not let out as much blood as you wish, then apply the flame directly to that small opening; and work gently, so that the part may be swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the area swollen, do not re-open the wound, and place a poultice of lard on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the lard that is in the oil; and thus administer the lard of oil in every wound that you open veins to stop the flow of blood; and it also makes a triaicle and bowels of them when placed on the area; and it disperses the blood subtlely when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not bled before and the opening of the vein is small, hurry and place a sponge soaked in warm water on the area and bind it for an hour; and you should do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains in the area after a few days, some blackness or greeness appears, it does no harm; and if you see anything, place some aloe or myrrh made into a poultice, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and appearance at the opening of the basilic vein: put your hand over it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So be sure not to put anything on it from what we have said, for it might cut into an artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its quantity and the nature of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it is thinned out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for those who are full and swollen, and need bloodletting, that one makes them a larger wound, and the fleams must be wide; and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and they should be bled little and often, and one should bleed them by cutting across, not puncturing; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood flow and nerve damage, and is better than bleeding from a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those whose body needs bleeding, one should give them moist bread in pomegranate juice; if they are hot-tempered, they should eat it three or four times before bleeding. And if of a cold complexion, they should eat moist bread in muscat syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and nuts, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during bleeding, after a large amount of blood has been lost, he should drink broths and subtle fragrant syrups, and use the other remedies we have mentioned in the chapter on syncope, for the opening of the veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to open his arm and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by significant bleeding, that he bleeds a little at a time according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to open their arm after the first bleeding, and they have a strong body, then heal for .7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the new hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed elsewhere, then they should bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is a lot of blood inside the body that has been heated and causes fever; therefore, you must draw off a large quantity and widen the opening so that it drips out gently; then you should check all the conditions for bleeding, and place your hand on his pulse as he bleeds, so that death does not come to him through the vein, and this often happens when the surgeon is negligent; and you must not press hard on the vein when you see the arm being released and bleeding again, and the opening is closed; nor if it is crooked, should you straighten the arm suddenly, for that would be harmful; but let it be until it bleeds a second time. Then you can apply the fire to the tip, so that the frozen blood inside the vein melts and drips out, and place a little warm water on it, pressing gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it at all, until the abscess has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.Et se li sang est rouge, si est bon signe; et s’il est sanz couleur, si est mal signe.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are bled in the place of the vein in the head because it is composite.Et li voinne emmi le bras et le chief sont sainie en leu de la veine emmi la face.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient places his hand in hot water until the vein turns red; then tie it loosely so that the vein appears well, then bleed now from the middle, not from the broad or long vein; and let the incision be wide, and let the bleeding be close to the joint of the hand, and if none can come out, put the hand back in hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is in winter, do not return the hand to hot water, because we put it in there more in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than from any other vein because there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Bleeding from the vein on the little finger of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: straighten the hand, put in hot water until the vein swells, so that one can see it; and if you bleed from the middle, and if you cut it from top to bottom, it will not hurt; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are completely naked under the skin; then put the hand back in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as necessary, then place oil and silk on the vein to heal quickly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the right side, and do everything as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the sophia is good for all diseases that are beneath the body, such as diseases of the chest, and retention of fluids, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its salve are such that the patient should soak their feet in hot water, and rub the salve on the vein until it disappears, and apply it above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and up the foot, they should apply it to the largest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and treat it across as well by cupping; and let the flames be anaesthetized.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the poison cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the salve does not work the first time, they should try again the second day, for the area is salty; and do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and similarly make the sophia salve for the other foot in the same way.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its remedy is worth the pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its healing is such that the patient enters the bath, and twists his ankle three times, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then heal it in every way you can, and by crossing over; and it is better that you cover it, for the part is safe, and it is very relaxing for many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not believe this, then heal a vein on his back which opens towards the small toe, and guard against the nerves; and make the blood flow as much as you can see, and then loosen the bandage and place cotton on it and tie it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made from horns, or copper, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done by burning is done in two ways: with fire or without; and the cupping that is done by burning and by bloodletting is performed at 14 places on the body, one of which is on top of the head; and another on the neck; and two more on either side of the neck; and one under the chin; and one on each shoulder; and one on each hip; and one on each thigh; and one on each ankle; and the cupping does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this it does not weaken at all, as is done with bloodletting; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of sickness it is needed to bleed, or because of habit, we should do so every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and throughout the entire year; for there are those who, when they need to bleed, become heavy-headed; and there are those who experience puffiness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue swells, and they taste blood; and there are those who faint, and see blackness and horror and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is during the moon month, we command them to fast after the third hour of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with headaches ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this venting is in place of the bleeding of the head, and it should not be used by those of a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, for it does them great harm; and for this reason the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases in their heads.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal from it become oblate, and because of this, the cupping glass should be placed a little lower to guard against oblateness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation in the neck is in the place of the artery of the head and the basilic vein, and because of this it helps with swelling in the feet, and with fissures in the ducts of the lungs, and with cough and with repletion; and one should not push on it too much, for if it is pressed too hard, it can cause obstruction in the gullet or stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilations in the two collar bones of the neck help with headaches and eye pain and migraines, and with strangulation and toothache, and are in the place of the artery of the basilic vein; and you must instruct the surgeon to express his hand when placing it, so that he does not compress the artery and cause a gushing of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Wind beneath the chin causes disease in the mouth and corruption of the gums and similar diseases which affect the mouth; it occurs at the point where the two lips meet.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Wind at the shoulders causes a disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilations in the armpits are like three veins in the arm, for they attract blood from these large veins; and instruct the surgeon not to push too deep, for under the skin there are nerves and arteries.Li ventosations as coutes si valent as voinnes dou poing, et as nervs qui vont a la main, et covient que li sainor les ventile, car il adest souvent que ilz sont estraintes et dolors; si li sainor veult ventiler li ners desom, qu’il le fies desoz le peele de la main.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass placed on the back is effective for hemorrhoids and diseases underneath; and it should be large and made of brass, so that it can effectively draw out fluids; and in some cases, if it is too small, it may break and cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg cupping-glasses heal openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains in the joints, and of the muscles, and of the bladder, and they realign the bones; and they are placed on the two thighs, and on the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after a long time, and bring on fainting in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping-glass is that you first place it empty, and suck gently, and place it quickly, and move evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and the redness of blood appears; then stop, and replace the cupping-glasses, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have such thin skin and small pores: so one should only strike once, and make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to sottily open the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw blood a little at a time, we only need to strike once.Et se li sans est clers et legiers, si covient ferir .iiij. fois soulement: la premiere fois si est por subtiliier la voie dou sang, et les autrs si son por sucer.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If we want to draw a lot of blood, we should leech often; and if the blood is thick, we should pierce with a needle, and the spots where the needles enter should be such that the heart is suddenly pierced, and it suits those who have tough, hard skin and narrow pores that you anoint the places on the leeches with aperitif and dissolving oils: if it is in the winter, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in summer, with watercress oil, or lily oil, or camomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsamite, or oil of aniseed, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if they to whom one bleeds have soft skin and wide pores, then no oil should be put on them, but they should be washed after bleeding with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have a lot of moisture, it helps to rise with garlic, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities are raised by old wine, or by water of succus, or by the infusion of fennel or chamomile, or other similars; and one should not bleed with a cupping-glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after venting the wind, and it is necessary that he warm himself when he is to be bled and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the person who is bleeding is choleric, and if the blood is too thin and inflamed; then one should eat cool things, like pomegranates and endives and lettuce with garlic, and similar things; and small amounts of porridge, and milk, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cool complexion should drink honey syrup, and moderately old wine, which is between old and new, and eat porridge, and small amounts of porridge and peas and small birds; and on the day that one bleeds, one should drink more than eat; and it is good to give some men theriac or musk before bleeding, or afterwards, to strengthen the main organs; and dilute the blood, but one should not drink this who are hot-tempered.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are placed without causing harm are those that are placed on the liver, and on the mumps, and on the gout, and on the belly, and the armpit, and the ribs, and the hip; for these members do not endure being hurt upon the eyes, and it is only done in order to draw blood from one member to another, as we place them on the breasts when the nipples are healthy; to remove the viscousness that is in the member, as we place cupping glasses on the belly and armpit to reduce the member; and it removes pain when there is inflammation or a stone, and by its attractive power perhaps draws out the inflammation, or the stone deserts its place; and thus does it act when it is placed on the liver and on the mumps when there is retained windiness, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the fire-cupping instrument is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it is two inches wide and half a palm deep, and on the sides around the middle there is a small hole, just big enough to push through a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of brass or iron, to hold a candle, and they are both large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who use them; for the ventouses of children are different from those of the elderly, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And you should place this ventouse on the limb thus: take the candle of wax or the linen and put it inside the ventouse through the bar in the middle, so that the flame is at the bottom of the ventouse and does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, and hold your fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when you wish, the vapors will go, and you remove the ventouse; then take the linen as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	Therefore in the cupping-glass which is administered for pleurisy, in all acute diseases, there is no tube or opening, and it is not removed until it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb only; and that is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are not removed until they are in the soft water, without any porridge, and it is not administered unless there is room for a cupping-glass because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in naked flesh, such as fingers or nose, and others like them; and the quality of their use is that when you find leeches that are in soft clean water without any porridge, take them; and put them into fresh water for as long as they become familiar, so that there is nothing in their stomachs; and then let him be bled from a vein and with a cupping-glass, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place leeches on top of it; and when they are full, and bleed, if there is a place where a cupping-glass can be placed, let them do so, for it does much good.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, he raises the vein with ash and then water, then squeezes it; and if the vein heals too close to the body of the leech, he soaks a linen cloth in cold water and places it on top until the leech is suffocated; and if the bleeding increases, he applies ground vitriol, or galena, and similar substances, until it is stopped; or he places half a handful of peeled beans on the vein, and leaves them until they warm the spot, which will then stop the bleeding; and if he needs more, he takes other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches will not attach, he rubs the bleeding spot with fresh blood, or he inserts a needle so that the blood flows out, and then applies them; and as soon as they taste the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they defecate, he puts on a poultice of powdered aloes and salt, or ash, and they will soon stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is a cure for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish people are talking about this chapter, which they have never seen in any of the ancient books, nor have they read any letter; and for this reason, science is strange in our land, for I have never found any good ones; and I know nothing about it, except through the science of the ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have acquired knowledge, and through experimentation and the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue of this book the subjects of the discussion and the chapters where the sage places his understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing occurs in someone, you must hurry to heal the patient from both sides, if nothing else holds him back, such as weakness of the body, or youth, or old age; and if the weather is not very warm, or too cold; and eat cool foods, that is, cool joints, and bird and deer meat, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill himself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of a hot abscess, or of a spreading matter in the limb; then return the patient to his former lifestyle.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, one should feed the patient foods that promote swelling and viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testicles, feet, and belly of a cow, offal, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because with this swelling, the bones will be held together and heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well set or joined according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor those which are also too tender, such as the bones of small children; but have no concern about it, reset the broken bone with the large tendons that stretch and join the member together, so that it is forced into its former position; and do not stop at all in his work, and for this reason one should eat plenty of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you should know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the foot, or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another in piercing, just as in the cutting of a quill for writing.Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, then there is a break all over, like a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each bone has its own nature and its proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes into its place; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the joint is twisted, and it appears clearly by feeling, and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or feeling, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture; but there may still be a twist, or a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it by hand, but apply remedies that follow, and then hold it firmly yet gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes in the bone, and are the two parts separated, they should now be put back together evenly, so that the abscesses heal; and if the abscesses are hot, let them rest for a day, so that the abscesses can settle; then put it back into alignment as easily and gently as you can, and know that the restoration of the bone is easier than the restoration of the one with pieces; then hold it tight, as it should be afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces of bone, if it is in two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or your hand, if it is a small member, or with two tendons, or one tendon and your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, you bring them back together with all your strength, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient; and fit the two heads of the bone well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you can feel it with your hand if it seems to you that it is not in the right place; then dress it nicely, and do not pull on it too much or press as those who bring about hot abscesses and contraction in the limb by their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at rest, the patient must be instructed to keep it still, whether waking or sleeping, turning or otherwise; and he must ensure that the limb is so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, he is not at rest, and you must put him in such a position that he feels no pain; and you must ensure that he is straightened out so that no crookedness comes to him as he is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and hands and the like: these must be wrapped with soft, fine linen; and for larger ones, such as thighs and legs, use a wide, sturdy bandage, for wide bandages embrace the entire large limb and constrict it evenly all around, so that there is no swelling; then wrap lightweight bandages three or four times around the broken limb, according to its size, and tighten your hand slightly on the bandage as you go, then go over the break and ease up on the pressure, so that the break moves away slightly; then soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp most of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wrap it around the broken area again; then go back to the part below the break and constrict it gently, not too tightly or too loosely, as we have said in the first hour above; then place pieces of linen or bandages between the bandages so that they are all even, then tie everything tightly with a bandage on top, and then put your splints on well, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something warm upon the abscess to soothe it and reduce the swelling, and leave it thus for several days; then bind it tightly with bandages, and let them be of half a large cane, or of wood used for making clubs, or of palm fronds, and let them be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the bandage that one places upon the dislocation should be a little larger and broader than the others; and it should be as long as the limb is small or large; then tighten over the bandages as you did at first, then tie a thread over them accordingly, as in the first instance on the dislocation; the tighter underneath, the less above; and the thread must be fine, not too thick nor too thin, and it should be of soft linen; for if the thread is thick, as I have seen fools do, making their ligatures from twisted cords, and this is a great mistake, for the ligature cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it should not be more than two fingers' width between each bandage.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is nervous from the cold of the stars after their constriction in a healthy manner, then place beneath them pieces of linen or other soft material so that they are not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the bones are broken, I will describe the treatment for this below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should know that one must not dislocate all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the member is swollen, you should not put splints on it until after five or seven days, or more depending on the heat of the abscess; and here is the manner of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that is kept on the walls of the mill, and mix it with an abundance of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common way of the plaster restoring the fracture in various conditions, especially in women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster restoring fractures, dislocations and twists: take three parts of bark of willow, and alder, and elecampane, and asafetida, and gum arabic, each weighing 10 grains; myrrh and aloe, each weighing 5 grains; and alchangel, weighing 8 grains; and grind them into powder, and mix with egg white. If the person's complexion is warm, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is useful for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster that is good for torsion: take mastic and balms, each 10; myrrh and aloes, each 9; wax 6; Armenian bole 10, and grind well, and mix with water or an abundance of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones displaced from their places, and to soothe the resulting pain, and to treat the fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess and removing pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves, and leaves of the earth pebble, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture and to reduce an abscess: take new linen, and moisten it in vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, and wheat flour, one part each; grind them and cook in wine. If the member is inflamed, cook it in moist coriander water or water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another more powerful method of plaster, for when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.Take equal parts of the roots of marshmallow, camomile, and violet, and grind them with vinegar; cook in wine until thick. If the member is inflamed, cook it in moist coriander water or water, and apply it.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of comfrey, and the seed of flax, buckthorn, milk thistle, and yellow oxeye daisy, and the flowers of violets and chamomile, each one part; and grind them up, and cook with water or salt water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocrites says in his book that one should not put on the broken member for restoration other than a cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else; it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says one must put on the broken member, to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of making an ointment that helps with injury and pain: take mugwort and human hair cut short, or bird feathers, and bee's wax, and mix them together, and crush them, and make an ointment from it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after that, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is the bone moved from its place; if not, loosen it with your fingers for several days. And if pain comes to the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, hurry up and loosen it, and remove the ointment immediately; and take a light cloth, and sponge of sea water moistened in water, and apply it to the area until the itching stops and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, then place upon it a layer of dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it up on a nut, until you are sure there is no hot abscess; and let the inflammation of the member subside, and the pain be removed, then begin again with gentle massage, and a little ointment, and do not pull as hard as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, and you need ointment and binding, then restart it, just as you did at first.Et se il adonque s’en va par fin et est sainz, si mettous embaumeure de l’esguileure, si com tu as mist premierement; et se il a duré longuement et qu’il soit osté, si mist li embaumeure et li lien, si com tu as mist premierement.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If the limb does not show any of the signs we have mentioned, do not try to set it for three, four, or five days; sometimes even twenty days, depending on what one observes, until the fracture heals and the bone draws closer to the skin above; then restrain it more tightly than before, and increase its bulk as I have already said.
