If you see that the area is drying out more than it should, know that swelling cannot occur there; therefore, soak it with warm water every time you loosen it, and do this every third day, while reducing the pressure slightly; through this practice, swelling comes to the limb, and quickly heals what the foolish healers do, who straighten limbs but harm them: this is wrong, and their methods are feeble, and I see nothing good that comes of laxity or doing it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures, with different shapes and distinct causes. Some fractures are caused by the impact of a sword, breaking the bone all the way to the socket located under the bone, as happens with an axe or a club. This type of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts into the bone without breaking it, and this type of break is called 'absolute'; and the wound from these two breaks is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an impact with force, or splitting, or from the collar bone, or from falling on stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a fracture piercing to the membrane under the bone, or on top of it, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that is lodged in the bone as thin as a hair, and the crack is small, then this type of fracture is called "capillary". If the wound is made by stone, or by falling, or by similar objects, and pushes the bone fragment inside, and the site is chiseled like the way blacksmiths work on kettles; then it is called a "stone fracture".
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This happens more often to those with moist bones in the head, like children's skulls; and it occurs in all types of fractures when small fragments are dispersed like pebbles, and I will speak about this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by examining them closely, and through interrogation while the patient is stretched out, and by the discolored skin that appears above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary resemblance is known when, after exposing the bone and rubbing it gently, a black Bruch appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be aware of any bad symptoms, and if you see no evil signs such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsion, paralysis, fever, eyes popping out and reddening, and other similar things in various conditions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no terrible accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the new-born comes to you first, and it is winter, you should remove the foreskin before the fourteenth day that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spring, you should hurry to remove the foreskin before the seventh day, otherwise, the tissue under the foreskin will be corrupted and the accidents we have described will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone extends just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you should split the fractured part thus: and you must grasp the head of the injured person, and expose the bone in every way you can, and over the wound more gently than you can; and if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone, or a suppurating abscess, treat it with what is appropriate. Then fill the site with moistened fabrics in rose oil; let the wound rest until the suppurating abscesses are soothed, and ensure there is no further bleeding. Then begin to remove around the bone, and this can be done in two ways: one way is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various cuts, some narrow and some wide, and they are pointed and made of iron; and work lightly so that you do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, you must pierce it all around, so that you administer cauteries with a chisel, not so deep that they penetrate beyond the bone of the chest, and it should have a rim or .i. circle above the tip, which does not allow the tip to pass beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each one comes in its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have chisels for all tests; and this is the form of the .iij. ways of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the bone are that you put 1 chisel on the bone, and turn it with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the chisel somewhere else a little later, and do this all around, then cut into the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this most subtly and lightly, as we have said, so that you draw out the bone to your hand, or with one of the instruments that you have, such as tweezers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is appropriate to remove any roughness that remains on the bone with another instrument resembling an incision tool, but it should be thinner and more delicate than other incision tools; if any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with the instrument. Then dress the wound as we have described, with bandages and ointments.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is safer; he praises it highly, and his word is final.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a part of the bone where the open fracture is located; once you have exposed that area, place under the edge of this lenticular incisor, from which the shape of the instrument comes.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is ağe on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then hit with a small mallet above, so that you gently tap the bone all around, and be careful of the membrane that is underneath; if it adheres to the bone, loosen it gently, for the bone can be loosened without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is only cut slightly on the surface, and there are small pieces, then one must smooth that roughness, and remove the scales with a subtle razor, of which you should have several quantities, in order to use the most suitable one according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Take first a large razor, and then a more subtle one, and do not cease doing this until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle fractures, one must prepare the wound according to its nature; and this is not a matter that can be entrusted to someone who has not dedicated themselves to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is exposed, you should take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another piece of linen doubled in two or three layers, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it over the first piece of linen; and do this as gently as you can so that you do not burden the wound, then administer another bandage above, and do not tighten it more than is necessary to hold the wound; and leave it like this for a day or two, until the abscesses are relieved, then loosen it, and apply remedies such as lili roots, and flour of beans, and incense powder, and aristologus, and similar things; and from these ingredients make a powder, and place it over the wound, and administer more remedies that do not cause biting; and ensure that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any ointment on it, or allow any pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the membrane of the brain, it hardens and causes great harm; for when one applies something biting over the wound, it causes it to harden from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no evil accident comes to the patient, as we have said, for it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness does not come but only due to the medicine that has been applied, because such virtue it has, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil, and glue a cloth with it, and place it over the syphilis; then treat it in ways that are appropriate until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You should know that sometimes the two parts of the jaw are broken, one by itself, because they are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is pushed or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should boil your little finger or thumb, and place the equal break inside your index finger, and the foreskin over it, until the nail grows back according to its natural shape; and do this gently, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is on top of the nail and the fingers cannot reach the spot, then you should put it in the same way at the end of a thin rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, then do this in the same way, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the wound is healed, then boil a tent of linen cloth around the finger where the break is.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you attach another to another part, if the fracture is there; and let the tents be so thick that they fill the holes of the nails.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must wet the bandages with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that is good, but one should wet the bandages with egg white and flour; then leave the bandage until the bone is set and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one attaches goose feathers instead of tents, and wraps a cloth around it, and holds the fracture in place, and the patient blows among it; then do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if a hot abscess comes in the nose while you are operating on it, then put cerate or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a little diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no abscess, then apply a poultice made from flour of sorrel, and incense powder, cooked in egg white, then place light dressings on top, but do not tie the nipple; and if the fracture of the nipple is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then stitch the wound, and treat it with healing substances, and bind it up, as with poultices and ointments suitable for this purpose; and if there is no wound inside the nipple, then treat it with bandages, and apply splints of soft wood, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated underneath, and there is no external wound, and the joint is only slightly displaced, without being broken in two, they know it easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the dislocation is on the right side, you should put your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the dislocation is on the left side of the jaw, then put your index finger from your right hand, and gently push the joint back into place, and hold it steady with your other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the dislocation of the jaw is displaced in , you should administer an extension of , so that it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement in the teeth, or looseness, then hold them with a gold or silver or silk thread; and put cerate on the broken jaw, and put on a double cloth; and put on top of the cloth a large well-made splint, or a piece of leather the same size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it on as tightly as possible, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the face changes, then loosen it after three days and then reset what has changed; and put an ointment on top of the powder from the mill with abundant egg yolk or flour of sisament, after removing the cerate; and put a thin linen cloth on top of the ointment, and if the ointments become hot, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it takes to heal; often it is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if painful abscesses come, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of bone is dislodged; then remove it skillfully with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains nothing inside, then stitch up the wound, if it is large, and place upon it suitable poultices to promote healing as long as necessary.
de la forcele	of the armpit:
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The armpit dislocates in several ways forward towards the shoulder, and there are three types of dislocation: it can be broken and separated into two pieces, which is the easiest to treat; or it can be broken with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when the fracture is without wound, that you have .ij. ministers, so that one holds the shoulder which feels the broken bone; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then place the break evenly in your hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is no appearance or displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch further, place under the shoulder of the patient a round pillow of cloth or wool, and make it thick according to your need; then raise and lower the bone, and press the pillow against your hand, so that you place the break evenly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the bone out of joint because it comes in too deeply, then the patient should lie on his back, and place under the shoulder a small pillow, and the ministers press the shoulder upwards, until the bone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then press the break with your hands, and if you find it splintered, you should split it; and draw out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any protrusion, then cut one of the incisions that you have made deeper, but place this instrument under the bone to guard against the sinew:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and resembles a spoon, and is not hairy, and is as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and has two heads, as you can see, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, as is the edge of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the edge is small, or if you doubt a hot abscess, cover the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, soak 1 bandage in rose oil and in garlic and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The dislocation of the bone, when there is no wound or cut, is to put on the bone the poultice of mill powder and egg white, and place light sponges on top, and if necessary, place a spike under the splint; then take a very large band one palm wide, then place a double draping over the sponges and the poultice; then take a thin strap three fingers wide and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs loose; and place the strap over the fracture, and wind the bandage over the collarbone and under the healthy shoulder blade, and under the affected shoulder blade; and adjust it from each side, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture in place, and you clearly see that the strap is not moving over the broken bone, then remove it every day, and when the ligature loosens, apply a restraint; and let the patient lie on his back, and while he sleeps, place a small pillow under the shoulder blade to raise the shoulder; thus the dislocation of the collarbone will be healed by the stretching of the shoulder, or you may bind the arm to the neck for up to 28 days if no bad accident happens; then start the poultice again if you see that it is needed, and stretch and leave it as such until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Then the shoulder may be broken or widely displaced without causing pain to the patient except through touch; one should set the fracture according to its shape and realign it in every way possible; then apply a powder of eggshell with egg white, and light poultices, and place a double drape over it; then put on a broad and thin splint, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there is any hair underneath the shoulder, use a cloth of linen poultice so that the splint lies evenly; then tightly bind it with a large bandage, so that the splint does not move from its position, and check the bandage each day; and every time it loosens, tighten it again, and adjust the splint if it has moved out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; the shoulder will be healed in 20 to 25 days. And when this time is up, remove the bandages, for it is not a bone that can be easily set right again.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out in front, and not under the heart, cut it away and do what we have said about the dislocation of the shoulder to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the dislocation of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The nose is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it often breaks at the bridge.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines downward, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks breath, and feels faint, and perhaps vomits blood, and the brain shows through the broken bone, and he feels very ill.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is to have the patient lie on their back, and place a cushion between their shoulders, then press their shoulders, and bring together the ribs on both sides with your hands, and carefully adjust them so that the bones are in the correct position; then apply poultices and bandages made from the subtle salt, or another light substance, and wrap it up in a cloth, and tie it onto the broken bone so that it does not move; then turn the leg gently to the side, and bind it firmly but comfortably, and check every hour if it has softened, and if it has, bind it more tightly; and if it needs to be loosened due to corrosion or itching that comes to the area, or pain or an abscess, then do so quickly, and loosen the bandage, and clean away any pus that has formed, and apply remedies to treat the area; then reapply the poultice, and bind it up tightly until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs only occurs in the large ribs near the back, and in the chest area, and they only bend due to their being slippery; and it feels good when pressed on both sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the ointment, and bind it with a bandage, if necessary.Et si li estele ne tenet pas, si covient que tu le baisies de vives coles, si com il convient, et met l’estelle sus, et ainsi le laisses.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is declined inward, the patient feels great pain and puncturing, as with pleurisy, for the bone pierces the membrane; and he also has pain in his arms and chest and vomits a large amount of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancients have given it great importance.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that bloat the belly in order to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not believe that hot abscesses will come, unless they have already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if he has come, then heal him.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should place cupping glasses over the area to draw out fluids, and that this is sensible advice; nevertheless, there is a doubt that the cupping glass might attract excess fluids to the site due to the weakness of the patient.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one must cover the area with moist woolen cloth in hot oil, and place tenting between the ribs to apply pressure evenly all around; then it should be bandaged with a pleurisy poultice made of meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure through the bone which points to the webbing, and there is doubt in the patient, then one should split above the location of the broken rib, and one must place an instrument underneath to push out the pleura; and then one must chip away at the bone, and gently pull, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses arise, one should place wet rags in rose oil and apply them to the area; and treat the location where the abscess is needed, and let the patient lie carefully on his side where it is, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a fracture of the bones of the neck, and it sometimes bends; and also of the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if you see his hands become soft, swollen, and dead-feeling, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick him with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	You know that they are deadly in many dispositions, and if they move and feel good when one pulls and pinches them, you know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the ailment is healed, if one applies a cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, then take note if the feet are numb, and if the sensations are in the arms and on the back there are twitches and flatulence without will; and when one presses on his belly, there is flatulence without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is pressed on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.And if it happens that he cannot move one of his limbs, or both, and you see that he cannot move his arms or legs, or one side more than the other, then know that this is a bad sign.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	You know it is deadly if there is no progress in his healing.And if he has a fever for many days and nights, and does not want to drink or eat anything, but only wants to sleep, then know that this is a bad sign.Saiches qu’il est mortelz: car il ne vuit boire ne manger.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to them, then the thing is much easier.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is a hot abscess, then the physician should put rose oil or chicken egg white on the spine until it is soothed, then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters and bind it with a bandage; and he must command the patient to rest and not sleep on the painful side until it heals.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is exposed, then it must be covered with a cloth; and remove the bone, then join the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a single stitch, then the physician should apply ointment around the wound, until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the 'head of the shoulder', squeeze your left testicle in your left hand, and the right one in your right hand as much as you can, then apply the plaster and bandage, if necessary; then hold it tight, and if there is an exposed bone, cover it, remove it, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break in the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Then the bones of the hip may be broken, and if so, there will also be a little lessening in the head; they are long and sloping towards the buttocks, and the patient feels pain and piercing in the affected area, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over the fracture so that you are on the break; and you know where the fracture is and what its shape is; and if the fracture is only in the head, then put it back into place so that it is restored to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it slopes downward, then let the patient lie on his stomach so that the restoration of this fracture may be prepared for.Et se il decline ou pardeins, si fai gesir sur son dos, et tant li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie; car ele ne doit pas decliner a l’un cotez ne au chief.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it back into place, then apply the plaster, and then put on a splint of wood or horn, and bind the fracture so that it does not move; and press on the area under the ribs so that the clavicle is restored.Et si le malaide ne peut demorer sou la estele, si met le sur une table ou un leu plan, et tant li restoration soit aparillie.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if pus-filled blisters appear, do not touch them until the pus-filled blisters have drained and dry up, and then apply what we have said before; and then return to the healing process, and bind it as it should be, if there is no bad outcome; and that is how it's done.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoire is what is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two methods: one method is that you take a stick, smooth and straight, according to this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And take two chairs, and lean them against each other, and seat the patient on one chair; then let him stretch his broken arm out over the top of the chair, so that it hangs down, and place a cushion under his hand; then lean him back against something heavy or have someone hold him upright; then place the mirror so that the break aligns with his hands, so that the bone returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	Another method is to have the patient lean back against his heel, and tie his hand to his neck; then instruct two ministers, one to hold what is above the break in place with their hands, and the other to hold under the elbow, and each to stretch their respective parts.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more severe, then pull the ligament beneath the fracture and above it, and stretch each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then you should put the ligament under the socket and the other towards the neck, under the fracture; and likewise, if the fracture is towards the neck, then it is necessary to put the ligament lightly and without labor, so that the fracture is even on its place, and on the neck; then put the fracture evenly as it should be, and hold it, if no abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess forms, do not tighten it for seven days, and put cool linen in vinegar and rose oil over the abscess until it is soothed; then tighten it, and the method of tightening is that you put the plaster over the break, then assemble the arm over the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and lay a cloth and tighten over the shoulder and arm so that the arm is straight, without anything bending it or the bone moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will move, use pins and place a pin larger and stronger than the others on the fracture, with .1 inch of space between each pin, and let each pin be large enough to project .3 inches beyond the fracture on either side; then pull on the pins, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the fracture, strongly and without moving them too far.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the settlement of the stars, and the binding, as we have said, at the time that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, then leave it to ligature until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the ligament every three days so that itching or swelling does not come to the place, or the nutrients cannot come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you follow these instructions, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if such accidents do not occur, and the dislocation does not return until after three days or more, let the patient sleep on his back, and keep his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder a cushion filled with wool, equally thick all around, and every hour of the day and night, see that the figure of the broken member does not move, nor the ligaments soften; then he will be adjusted by medicine, and given the food we have previously mentioned, so that the food is in the first subtle state; and when he begins to recover, let him eat solid food.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be adjusted within 40 days of the injury; then they should be reset, and baths and ointments administered to adjust the joint.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is bad and obstructed, it will remain unhealed for 1 or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	of the elbow
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of 2 bones, which are called the 'ulna', one of which is small and sits below the armpit; and the other is larger and sits below the little finger. Sometimes only the larger ulna breaks, or the smaller one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, their restoration and healing is easier; but when the large bones are broken, healing is more difficult and takes longer than when they are broken all at once.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bone that is broken, then one should gently extend and align it.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, then one should apply more force in extending it; and lay him on his back, with his affected arm raised higher than the rest of his limbs, and his small fingers lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross his legs over himself, and a pillow under his head to elevate it, so that the patient does not experience any discomfort; then one minister should extend the affected arm upwards towards the hand, and another minister upwards towards the elbow.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts the mirrors equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are pieces in the fracture, put each one in its place, and if none are out of place that press the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before, on the chest and the bone.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a particular chapter; so take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, then glue a bandage of cerate made of rose oil and white wax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the bandage subtly over them, until the hot abscesses are eased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerate, and apply the plaster of flour from the mill with an egg white, then put on the bandages, and let the bandage over the fracture be stronger, and a little larger than the others; and know that there should be 6 bandages on the arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and press harder on the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as time goes on, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages over the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread by which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reexamine the limb and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching coming to the limb, then you should wash the limb with hot water until the itch is relieved; and let the limb not be pressed or restrained while resting.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then restart the stretching, and if the joints are relaxed and the bones are dislocated, or anything similar, then adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you are unable to bring the nutrients to the member because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little bit, and leave it like that for a few days, until the nutrients flow, and then stretch it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have mentioned happen to the patient, then do not release him until 20 days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or if he feels pain in his neck and shoulders, then he should sleep on his back with his neck aligned, and guard against movement and convulsion; and know that this fracture will be healed within 30 or 35 days, or perhaps within 20 days, depending on the constitution and the individual's natural healing process.
de la brisure de la main	of the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and at the knuckles there are few fractures, and only sprains many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, then the patient should cross his arms, and sit upright facing forward; then he should extend his affected hand onto a flat surface, and the assistant should extend the broken bones and set them straight, making sure they are well-aligned; then apply the plaster and dressing, if there is no abscess, and then put on a splint according to the size of the limb; and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the side of the palm near the belly, make a splint out of fabric, and instruct the patient to squeeze their broken hand; then wind a long strip of cloth around it, and the splint should be made of soft wood as large as the palm of the hand, and bound tightly in place, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the back of the hand, then you should put one splint above and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to one of us in the hand, whether it is the palm, he puts it equal, as it should be; and he presses it with the palm, and if you see, put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as in the index or one of the others, he makes it equal, and binds it with the healthy finger that is next; or you bind them all together, holding them steady, or you put a splint on, as in the palm; and take care in the restoration and in the preparation of hot abscess, and heal what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and one can see it well when it turns forward and backward; and its restoration is that one binds one ligature above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then he extends each ligature to his part equally; and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, then one of the ligatures should be towards the buttock, and the other ligature underneath the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then one ligature should be on the side of the knee and the extension should be down; then put the plaster on top of the bone so that it is level with its natural shape, and then apply the ointment, and the bandage, unless an abscess forms.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down, then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is made in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap a hard bandage twice over the fracture, and leave the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and tie a long string between the thigh and the leg underneath the knee, so that the end of the string comes out at the top; then go back up the leg and the thigh with the bandage, then put splints on top of the fracture, and put another splint on the bone of the leg; then tighten the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to make it even, then start tying three or four turns over the fracture; and the more you go up from the fracture, the less you should tighten it; then pull on both ends of the string that you tied between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are on top, then go back down to the bottom at the end of the string, so that it doesn't move from its place, then leave it like this, so that no abscess, swelling or anything else forms.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens that there is a piece of bone sticking out, it should be cut away if possible; and if not, then the area should be split open, and the wound treated as we have said many times before, until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken like when they put a stake in it, as in the shoulder and arm; all the same, with this restoration made, the patient does not improve.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you should know that the thigh is restored in one day, or a little less or more, according to the different complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the back of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the knee joint there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a slit, and it happens in every wound, whether there is feeling or not, and this is true for everyone.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts straight what is crooked at its joints, as much as it can be moved; then apply the plaster, and put on a round bandage if necessary, and bind it up as it should be; then follow all the directions we have given for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar conditions; and for each accident, do what is appropriate until the patient is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones; one is called the "mustelz" and the other the "foscile". Every kind of fracture happens in the leg as it does in the arm, and so its treatment is also the same, and all the procedures are the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns completely inside out.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, return above.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, great pain is felt, and it can be seen clearly; and it turns inside out.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, use extension, and set it straight, and bind the splints evenly; but still, if the fracture is severe and there are several pieces, then the extension should be lesser and gentler; and adjust it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, take two splints of wood that match the leg from one side to the other, and make them as long as the leg from the knee to below; then wrap two bands above and below, and tie it in the middle, and at this time the leg should not decline to the right or left, and thus it is well; and some administer a board as long as the leg, and it is made of wood, and they put the leg on it to prevent movement, and properly adjust that in the fracture where there is injury; and move the leg every day to see if there is any hot abscess or other accident; then cure until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of bone fractures of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	There is no fracture at the ankle, but sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot and in both feet, and there are only bruises with various dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot, and you see the bones sticking out above each other, then put the foot on the ground as if it wanted to walk, and then put your own foot on top of it, where the bones are raised; then press down on it until they return to their place. Then apply the ointment and bandages, and under the sole of the foot place a small wooden board with two pieces of wood attached, then tighten the foot with a bandage, and after you have wrapped it up with cloth and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find that the bones are healed, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are one or two broken bones, then treat them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the finger, and let it be a little wider, then put under the foot that small board which I mentioned before, and tighten it in place; and if there are one or two, or more, broken bones, then place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen, and tighten the board under the foot; and let the top of the board press hard against the sole of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, since we have spoken of them; and treat each case as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone in the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of a woman's nature are broken, have her sit up straight, then lean her towards her back, and hold her from behind. Then fill the opening of her nature with cotton, and insert as much as a finger; then make the woman stand up, and gently lift her back little by little, and the cotton will pop out as it reaches the entrance of her nature, and the bones will return with the finger. And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days; the fracture will be restored. If you wish, take a goat's bladder, tie a cane to the opening, fill the bladder with air by blowing into the cane, and the nature will return the fracture. Then fill it with cotton and leave it for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the man's or woman's elbow is broken, restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip; and these breaks are not hidden from those who put their study and skill into it, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaks indicate in many ways the right way to restore them; understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gullet and fill it with the penis; then wrap cloth around it tightly, and leave it for three days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	from breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as in the thighbone or shoulder, that he be treated immediately according to the remedies we have described earlier.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then restart the treatment for the fracture in that very hour or that day, if no abscesses have formed.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if deep abscesses arise, let the healing be until the tenth day, until the abscesses are settled, and do not touch them on the third or fourth day, for you would bring about an evil occurrence.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the uncovered heart, then you should gently put it in place with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not apparent to you in putting it equal with your hands, then use this instrument which is made of iron and is seven or eight inches long, and its width according to the quantity of the wound; and for this, the needle must be taken by the surgeon so that he requires three or four of them for each cure of a fracture; and it should be round and somewhat thick so that it does not bend under pressure on the member during your work, and should be tapered at the front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
