Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the curved shoulder should be placed on top of the visible bone; and the joint is reset once, so that it comes back into alignment.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is small, and the instrument cannot grip the bone well, then you must chip away at the head of the bone until the instrument can hold it.Et se li brisure est granz et li os est fends a longue traie, si covient que tu la remets sus le chief de l’os apparent, et tu le boutas tant qu’il soit igal; car le chief de l’os qui est apparant n’a point de force ne de substance.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot pull the bone back, as we have said, use an appropriate tool, whether a knife or a probe, to your ability; then remove what is stuck in the bone with scrapings and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Then do this so that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth with red wine, and carefully if it is on the wound; and do not put cerot or anything else containing oil on it, so that porridge and corruption does not come to it; then administer the ointment when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the surrounding area according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not pressed by the bandage; and many times people have done this foolishly, and have brought upon the patient either death or corruption; and let the constriction be softer and gentler than other bandages.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may come to it, as we have said, and you feel pain in the area, then do not put ointment on it; but wrap around it, instead of ointment, hard pieces of cloth, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the wound swelling, then remove what you have placed over it completely, and apply ointment that heals wounds, such as tetrafarmacon and similar remedies.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you should loosen the member twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and closed up.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And one must arrange the limbs so that the bow runs smoothly downstream.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they persist for many days and it cannot be welded but keeps slipping back down the bow, know that there are small pieces of bone causing this, so you should probe the wound with a tent and remove all the dislodged pieces causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula or any other form of corruption appears, then you should treat it according to what he said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and protruding from the limb, such as in the thigh or shoulder, and similar large limbs, do not treat it, for many die from it, but leave it alone until it closes over after 20 or 30 days; then cure the wound if you can, and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	brus
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	There often comes after the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, an ugly sight to see the deformation of the limb; and sometimes the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the patient has diarrhea: administer astringent medicines such as aloe, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolla, mixed with wine, egg white, or garlic; place them on the navel in poultices, and keep them firmly in place for several days; then remove them and repeat until the swelling goes down. Alternatively, apply a piece of well-prepared plaster to the area, as plaster has the property of drawing out inflammation from the limbs; if the swelling has become hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed, cut away the surface, and draw out the excess material; or have someone else scrape away at it until it is gone, and then heal it.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weakened after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and the limb remains weak and fragile, this can happen for several reasons: it could be because it was bound too tightly and not properly aligned, or because there were too many ligatures that prevented proper circulation to the limb; or due to excessive swelling, or too much movement before healing was complete; or because there is a lack of blood in the body, which causes weakness.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you cause the patient to eat and make the body tender, so that blood multiplies within him; and the provider bathes him, and gives him joy and relaxation; then put pitch on the limb, so that the pitch attracts the great heat, and often sprinkles it with lukewarm water, until the heat penetrates the limb; and he returns to his natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the limb crooked after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are crooked after healing, and the broken bones are open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless, it does not lose its natural function: therefore do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the limb completely anew; many fools have done this in our land; and these actions are blamed, and great harm results, and sometimes death; nevertheless, if the dislocations and torments are fresh, they should be sprinkled with lukewarm water, or herbs that soften, such as marshmallow leaves, and roots, and meadow-sweet, and similar medicines that soften; and you make a soothing ointment, such as well-prepared diaquilon, and you take the mucilage of marshmallow, and cook it with sheep tallow or sisimint oil, and make an ointment for it; or you take fat figs, and grind them with colon dung, and similar medicines that soften.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the dislocation is reduced by continually rubbing with moist hands.Et se il adontent est si grant dolor, ke li malaide ne pues demorer, si convint que tu le traies a la plaitre; car en ceste maniere li malaide deffaut plus tost et li dolors sont moult meins.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And movement must be brought to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosities are hardened like stone, and it is necessary to open them with an iron instrument, then they must be cut into gently with a subtle incision, and put cotton and study into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.Et de cest dislocation il y a grand douleur et grant lesion por coi il faille estude et science.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	And of this dislocation there is great pain and great injury, therefore it requires study and knowledge. When dislocation comes to someone, they must be reset without delay.Et si li membres est desaloiez, il covient le remestre a son leu;
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the place will swell and perhaps return to its place with difficulty; therefore, one must not move it at the hour when it is swollen: many times it brings on swelling and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient be bled, then let him rest until the abscesses are soothed; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then reset it gently, and cure each member as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the head up to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Then the jaws become dislocated, and both dislocations occur in two ways: they are slightly displaced from their place and softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging down towards the feet, and saliva flows from the mouth so that it cannot be held closed, nor can the tongue be wrapped around words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it will return to its proper place through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is entire and accomplished, then you must reset it hastily without tarrying; and in such a way that the minister holds the head of the patient and puts his thumb of one hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and let the other fingers be spread out to make it even; and command the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And she looks at it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the reset is painful, especially when both mandibles are together, then treat them with hot water and oil until they are reset lightly; do not touch or move the jaw, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back equally and the mouth of the malady is closed well without softening, then put on dampened cloths made into a poultice of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his head should be between two pillows so that he does not move it to either side, nor strain to yawn, but take light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws are bound and healed. Then he may eat whatever he wants lightly, and not exert himself to open his mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well bound and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset within an hour and are not converted to their place, then fever and usual sickness come, and perhaps stomach problems, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is deadly; and many die from it within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislodge it from within the chest and the abdomen; it is sometimes dislodged by force, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies consistently on his back and extends his arms; then press the dislocated area with your palm firmly, and it will return to place; then put on the poultice and bandage, and bind it tightly; and the shoulder joint near the neck cannot be dislocated; if it does become dislocated and returns to place once, then put on the poultice and bandage and bind it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed. In this way, the shoulder joint is also returned to its place when it becomes dislocated from its position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You should know that the shoulder can be dislocated in three ways: one is when it dislocates at the bottom near the armpit; the second is near the foot; and occasionally it dislocates at the top, though this is rare. It does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; often it dislocates below towards the armpit, especially in those who are thin, for in them it pops out easily; but in those who are plump, it pops out and goes back in with a little effort.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, some men experience a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must test it to make sure, and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And you will recognize a downward dislocation when there is an obvious difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one; you will find a pit at the top of the shoulder, and underneath the armpit at the top of the shoulder, it will look like a hole; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose nor move in any way. And if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden but obvious at the touch; this kind of dislocation does not need to be reduced when new, unless the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the assistant to lift the sick hand up, then place your knees under the shoulder, and pull the joint firmly upwards in its place; and the assistant lifts the hand and stretches it up, then places it down again; this will correct it quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and they should be given softening and soothing ointments, such as decoctions of alder and fenugreek and meadow sweet in water, and they should be eased; then the patient should be laid on their back, and a layer of wool equal in thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed underneath the shoulder, and the minister should place his heel on the sto, and lift the top of the shoulder gently, and pull the hand of the affected side; and another minister should hold the top of the affected shoulder so that it does not move downward; the shoulder will return right away, and you should do this according to this manner: and you should have a man present who is larger than the patient; he should stand straight toward the side, and push his shoulder underneath the affected shoulder, and lift the affected shoulder up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister should pull the hand of the affected side downward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the pain is too slight, then one can place something heavy upon it, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And one can reset it in another way also: take a long, pointed stake and push it into the ground so that the shoulder is as wide as a fist, but not too thick or too thin; then place it underneath the patient, but with a cloth over it, and let the patient's arm hang down on the other side; then extend their hand downward on the other side, and the joint will return to its place suddenly; and if it does not return despite all these things that we have said, then perform this treatment: take an iron stake two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a pointed tip so that it can be pushed into the ground, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie it onto the tip of the shoulder with soft cloth so that the shoulder does not bleeds the patient; then place it under the armpit of the patient; and extend his arm above the shoulder, and tie the shoulder to the arm, and the arm to the head of the hand; then place the arm on a small log, and extend the hand downward, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever way it may be, you must place under the armpit a woolen ball equal in size, then apply the prepared ointment of mill-powder, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it; then tighten it under the armpit gradually, and tie the string over the ointment, and hold the hand to his neck, and let the hand remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eats little, as long as the members are comfortable, for he will heal more quickly; and then eat more after .v. or .vii. days, and move him; and if he is stiff and not softened, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has been dislocated due to moisture or for some other reason, then you must administer cauterization at three openings, as described in the chapter on cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it still dislocates after 7 days, and the joint cannot hold, and he cannot lift his arm upward, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is torn or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fully healed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations that are towards the bottom, and in the breasts, or behind, are made by pushing and stretching with hands, and one administers to another; and treat it until it is healed.Li dislocation qui sont devers lou col, si doit on amener li col vers sou corps, et li membres vers le col, et li arces vers li membres, et li membres vers les arces, et li col vers les mameles; et si fait qu’il soit confortez.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb becomes lame and stiff with movement, then the patient should take many baths until the lameness is relieved and it returns to its former condition.
de la dislocation dou coute	about dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You should know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated by fingers, and it returns with fingers; and if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reset, for one can see and feel it well, and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick neck with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is broken, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you should reset it as soon as abscesses form, for if abscesses form, then it will be painful to reset; and by chance it may not be able to be completely reset, especially when it is in the back; so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and sometimes death ensues.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend his hand with your two hands; and let his arms be spread out, and his hands bent according to the joint, around, above and below, and push the joint towards his armpit together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he bends his hand towards his hand, and pulls from the root of the palm, the joint which has become dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it will not go back into place, then administer a strong extension; and while one minister holds the arm straight, the other minister bends the arm, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, then after you have wrapped a long, double cloth around it, and when the minister has joined the joint with his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint back into place firmly; and when it is in place, apply a dry plaster with egg white, and hold the arm firmly against the sick neck, and leave it for several days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, he removes the bandage and leaves it; and if you see that the joint is not healing well, he re-applies the plaster and the bandage, and leaves it for several days, until it is firmly in place; then he releases it.Et se li malaides a grant dolor en la jointe, si met sus une pomade que iloigne le calor et le doler, et puis le laisse.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels stiffness after the joint is moved and it moves, then bathe and rub it gently, and press until it is relieved; or put a pack of fat mutton on the joint, leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the pack back on, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see fit, put warm moist cow dung with butter on it, and apply pressure; then it will return to its natural state.
li dislocation de la main	dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is healed, and the return is lighter than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place gently, in the same hour that it was dislocated, so that the joint swells or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	The method of reduction is to put the affected hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and look at it and make sure it is even, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and bend it until it returns to its place; however, you should also check that it is in the right place. Then put the patient's back of their hand on a table for extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then the patient should lie with his back to the table, and the examiner puts his hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it goes back into place, that is good. If not, then strain it with soothing poultices on the hot abscess, and leave it like that without re-examining.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, then the joint will remain crooked; and it does no harm to the patient as long as his hand is weak and he cannot grip anything: so you should know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries; there is nothing else to do but to strain by cautery beyond the case, and perhaps nothing else helps.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, then put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then extract and let it be for five days, then loosen and leave it as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, then moisten with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.Et s’il a longuement demouré en l’estrain, si doit on li mettre la plastre sus le chiés et sus li col, car il est leus de l’un et de l’auter, si qu’il ne se puet bien demourer en l’estrain.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two hands
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the inside; then they are dislocated, and you must push the head of the finger towards the part where it is dislocated; and hold it there for two days, and then put it in line that day; and do not lie down, as we have said, and loosen it at night, and make him move it, and tie it during the day; and do this often, until it is healed; and do the same, when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from a dislocation of the shoulder blade from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade or collarbone is dislocated, there is no cure, for death comes quickly with this malady.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the excretions escape without willing them, and he cannot hold them in, and many times some members are weakened, or both hips or both arms or one; and many times the sciatica changes to four parts; that which changes in the back is called 'gilbositez': the cure is that you should find out if the gilbositez came from childhood: there is no cure or healing for it at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the old methods of cure described in great detail, but they did not bring much benefit in all cases; but I have abbreviated them according to my understanding and have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the sciatica which comes to the front, there is no cure or healing; and also that which comes directly to both sides, and cannot be cured without that which comes directly to the back, as I said; and it should be extended over its face in one place evenly, and it should not be twisted; then put a coal at the head in the ground, formed into a ball, and another at the feet; and tie a string under the sores of the disease, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers should hold the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the coals; and they should be well-fastened, the coals as we have said, and the minister should put his palms over the spine, until it eases.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, take a table three feet long, and lie beneath the wall, and let the patient be on their side, and place the head of the table beneath the wall; then put the middle of the table on the spine, and put the patient's feet on the other end of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place. And if you see fit, do it on the turn that turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should insert two brands at the head of the patient's arm, and two others near the feet, with a palm's width of space between each brand, both above and below; and let there be a hole in each brand for the rope to pass through, and fix the brands firmly in the ground so they do not move. And between each set of two brands, place a turning brand, over which the ropes will turn, and on each turning brand place a small brand a palm's width long, to guide the turn; then tie one end of the rope that is among the brands to the turn towards the head, and the other end of the rope towards the feet to the other turn, and all the ministers turn their turns to the whole rope, and the master puts the spine in an even position as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, then put on a desiccant plaster with plenty of egg white, and then the stumps, and then the stele of a tablet three inches long, which purples the area of the hunchback and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient's subtle cooling until he is healed; and if anything comes in the end of health, then one should administer softening and soothing medicines, with the stele that we mentioned above; and sometimes they administer a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes in the lower spine of the back, and they think it is dislocation; but it is the bone that appears, so one must not have any presumption about it: by chance it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come about as dislocations, and not as in other joints; and the joint of the hip is healed according to four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and mostly inside, and less healed in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased knee appears more than the healthy one, and the diseased one cannot bend his knee to the fire; and the part which is near is swollen with a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes from the inside out, it is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it comes from the outside in, are that his leg is well according to their appearance; nevertheless, he cannot bend his knee without pain, and if one makes him walk, he cannot go forward, and he holds back his urine, and the veins swell, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has it in the back are that he cannot bend his knee or double up, and that leg is more crooked than the other; and the groin is relaxed, and the head of the thigh bone is below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment for this kind of dislocation is that you examine whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its condition, and there is no treatment for it; and he must not be presumptuous.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for one in whom the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four kinds of dislocation, you should hurry to return the joint to its place, and stretch it in and out, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to its place, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, then you must prepare a strong minister and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or with one hand tied above the knee; and another minister stretches his hand above in such a way that he presses his hands under his heels, then he pulls him with a rope on the thigh; and another holds his head with a rope; and they all stretch upward and downward at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in four ways, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then the cure must be applied according to its likeness. When the dislocation is in the buttocks, you should support the patient on his healthy side, then tie the rope around the root of the thigh, and around the part below the anus; then stretch the rope upward toward the anus, and toward the scrotum; then have another minister grab his arms and embrace the thick part of the patient's thigh, and stretch it forcefully outward: it will return to its place immediately. This kind of dislocation is the lightest of all.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot bring it together in the way we have said, then you must tie the patient's two feet together with a strong leather thong above the heels and above the knees, and let the affected leg be stretched out two fingers more than the other; then let him be hung up by the head of a pole, and let his arms be two fathoms above the ground; then command a minister to hold the head of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the patient who holds the thigh firmly, for the joint will now return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is returned, let the patient lie as we have said in that which concerns gout; and tighten the thong on the affected leg properly, and also on the foot; then put two brands of fire, one at the head and one at the feet, and place the brand between the thighs of the patient in the form; and wrap moist cloths around it so that he does not scorch the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and let the surgeon hold the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it comes back, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table and press him as we have said in the chapter on dislocations, and lay the patient on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the leg slowly, and according to what I have said; and the helper puts his weight on the painful shoulder, then presses with the other hand, and pulls downward toward the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is on the side, he should not be stretched out flat or raised up from the bed, but he should be as if his hip were dislocated and he were lying on his sound side, as we have said in the chapter on lying down with a dislocated hip; and he should lie on his face, with the ligament stretched as we have said before, and someone should press on the joint against the table; and when the patient stretches out his legs and they are even, then draw the thighs together and apply the ointment and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then loosen it and put on the ointment again. And if you see that they are even, then bind it as before, and let him rest for another three days; then loosen it and let him walk comfortably until his limbs are healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to know, inside and outside, and behind; and does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not stick to his thigh, you know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit up straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee joint firmly; and another minister extends his foot so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it sticks well to his thigh lightly; and put the plaster on top, and make the leg warm at the thigh, and the ligatures together strongly for three days or four, then release it; and the patient should not work at all until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not at all, then administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes crushed, and sometimes completely dislocated, both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it hurts in front of the part where it is dislocated; the movements are light, and one should lightly extend it with their hands when it is only dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, then you should make the patient sit up straight, and hold his leg firmly by the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and press the foot firmly upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, by bending and stretching the foot; if it comes back, that is good; if not, then repeat the operation, for it will come back; and if it still cannot be reduced in this way, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix the strap firmly into the ground between his buttocks, and wind cloth around it so that he does not kick the leg; then one man holds the hip, and another stretches the foot upwards with their hands or with a cord tied to the ankle; then stretch each man equally, and the strap should be firmly between the patient's buttocks to hold him in place when you stretch; then put your fingers evenly over the dislocation with your hands, and another man holds the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at its worst, then put on the plaster and bandages, and bind it tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature softens, then bind it tighter; then loosen it on the third or fourth day, and let the patient walk in four days; and if he walks before that time, it is not certain that he will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a boil comes, you must calm it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the armpits
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the armpits are dislocated, they must be stretched without effort, and this is a minor issue.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the foot, you should have the patient sit on a flat surface or table, completely upright, and put your foot over what is visible of the joints, then press down firmly on your foot until it is restored; and when it is even and nothing is protruding, place a board with two notches under the sole of the foot, then bind it tightly, and leave it for three days, then loosen it; and let him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the cure, unless you are wise in the art and have long practiced it, and unless you are compassionate and merciful and cautious; nor should you be rash. And at the beginning use things that soothe a hot abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand if you see no hope of recovery; but when you do see hope, then immediately reset the limb to its proper place, so that the hot abscesses may heal; and once the limb is in place, administer soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and treat the wound as it should be treated with drying ointments; and if there is a fracture, and small bones are displaced, then set the bones, and do as we have said for simple dislocations; and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, for this will cause changes in your body according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body.
Amen	So be it.
